Tamattu' and Qiran for Makkans: The Hanafi Position
Hanafi ruling and dispute regarding tamattu' and qiran for residents of Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tamattu' and qiran for residents of Makkah, identify the Quranic proof (verse 2:96) and its interpretation, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A resident of Makkah cannot perform tamattu' or qiran — only ifrad is valid.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether the residents of Makkah and those within the miqat may perform tamattu' (combining Hajj and Umrah in one journey) or qiran (combining both with a single ihram). The Hanafi school, relying on the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:96) and the practice of the Prophet and his companion Ibn Abbas, restricts tamattu' and qiran to non-residents. The Shafi'i school interprets the same verse differently, allowing Makkans to perform these forms but without the obligation of a Hadi. We will walk through the dispute step by step.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the Hanafi school holds that tamattu' and qiran are not valid for a person whose family resides near the Masjid al-Haram (i.e., a Makkan or anyone within the miqat). Only Hajj ifrad is permissible for them.
This is a condition for validity, not merely a recommendation.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Locate the primary evidence: the Quranic verse (2:96) 'dhalika li man lam yakun ahluhu hadiri al-masjid al-haram'. The Hanafis interpret the word 'dhalika' (that) to refer back to tamattu' and qiran, thus limiting these rites to those not residing near the Sacred Mosque.
The verse is considered qat'i in thubut (certain transmission) but subject to interpretation (zanni in dalala).
3
Present the opposing school's view
According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik (in one narration), 'dhalika' refers to the Hadi (sacrificial animal), not to tamattu'/qiran. Thus, Makkans may perform tamattu' and qiran, but they are not obliged to sacrifice a Hadi.
The practical difference: in Shafi'i fiqh, the act itself is valid even without a Hadi.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the context of the verse and the reason (sabab) for tamattu' (deriving benefit from a single journey) do not apply to residents who are already present. Additionally, the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) and the fatwa of Ibn Abbas support the Hanafi view.
Ibn Abbas's report is cited to reinforce that tamattu' is only for non-residents.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Consequences: If a Makkan were to perform tamattu', according to Hanafis the act is invalid (batil) and does not fulfill the obligation of Hajj. According to Shafi'is, it is valid but without the requirement of a Hadi.
This difference directly affects the validity of the Hajj of a Makkan who attempts tamattu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۷۰۷ (۱۳) اہل مکہ کے لئے نہ تمتع ہے اور نہ قرآن ہے صرف ان کے لئے حج افراد ہے۔ (۱) آیت میں ہے ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام (ب) ( آیت ۹۶ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ذلک کا اشارہ تمتع اور اس کے تحت میں قرآن ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تمتع اور قرآن اس کے لئے ہے جو مسجد حرام کے قریب نہ ہو یعنی لکھی نہ ہو۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک مکی اور میقات کے اندر والوں کے لئے تمتع اور قران نہیں ہے (۲) ایک سفر میں حج اور عمرہ کر کے فائدہ اٹھانے کو تجمع کرنا کہتے ہیں۔ لیکن سفر ہی نہ ہو تو فائدہ اٹھانا کیا ہوگا۔ اس لئے اہل مکہ کے لئے تمتع اور قرآن نہیں ہے۔ حضرت عبداللہ ابن عباس کی یہی حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے حجتہ الوداع میں عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ ملا کر جمع کیا اور ہندی ہانکی اور ذی الحلیفہ سے ہدی ہانکی۔ اور حضور نے شروع کیا پس عمرے کا احرام باندھا پھر حج کا احرام باندھا اور لوگوں نے حضور کے ساتھ عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ ملا کر تمتع کیا۔ پس لوگوں میں سے کچھ نے ہدی کو ہانگا، اور ان میں سے کچھ نے ہدی نہیں ہانگا۔ پس جب حضور مکہ آئے تو لوگوں سے کہا کہ تم میں سے جس نے ہدی ہالگا اس سے کوئی چیز حلال نہیں ہوگی جو حرام ہوتی ہے جب تک کہ حج پورا نہ ہو جائے (ب) تمتع اس کے لئے ہے جو مسجد حرام کے قریب نہ ہو۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک آیت میں ذلک کا اشارہ تمتع نہیں ہے بلکہ ہدی ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک کی تمتع اور قران تو کر سکتا ہے البتہ اس پر ہدی لازم نہیں ہے۔ قال يحيى سئل مالك عن رجل ... وانما الهدى او الصيام على من لم يكن من اهل مكة (الف) (موطا امام مالك ما جاء فی التمتع ص ۳۵۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ یکی پر ہدی اور روزہ نہیں ہے۔
707 (13) For the people of Makkah, there is no tamattu' and no qiran; only Hajj ifrad is for them. (1) In the verse: 'That is for him whose family is not present at the Masjid al-Haram' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:96). In this verse, the indication of 'that' is tamattu' and under it qiran. Its meaning is that tamattu' and qiran are for those who are not near the Masjid al-Haram, i.e., not a resident. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, there is no tamattu' or qiran for the Makkan and those within the miqat. (2) In one journey, combining Hajj and Umrah and deriving benefit is called tamattu'. But if there is no journey, what benefit would there be? Therefore, there is no tamattu' or qiran for the people of Makkah. This is the view of Abdullah ibn Abbas. (a) The Prophet combined Umrah with Hajj in Hajjat al-Wada' and brought a Hadi from Dhu al-Hulayfah... then said: Whoever among you has brought a Hadi, nothing that was made haram becomes halal for him until he completes his Hajj. (b) Tamattu' is for those who are not near the Masjid al-Haram. According to Imam Shafi'i, the indication of 'that' in the verse is not tamattu' but the Hadi. Therefore, according to him, one can perform tamattu' and qiran, but the Hadi is not obligatory. Yahya said: Malik was asked about a man... and the Hadi or fasting is only for those who are not from the people of Makkah. From this athar, it is understood that for the Makkan, there is no Hadi or fasting.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether residents of Makkah (people within the miqat) can perform tamattu' or qiran. The Hanafi position, based on the verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:96) and the interpretation of Ibn Abbas, holds that tamattu' and qiran are valid only for those who do not reside near the Masjid al-Haram. For Makkans, only Hajj ifrad is permissible. The Shafi'i school, however, interprets the same verse differently: 'dhalika' refers to the Hadi, not tamattu', so Makkans can perform tamattu' and qiran, but they are not obligated to sacrifice a Hadi. The Hanafi school relies on the fact that tamattu' involves deriving benefit from a single journey, which does not apply to residents who are not traveling. The proof from Ibn Abbas's fatwa and the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) is adduced.

Key Terms
حاضری المسجد الحرام (ḥāḍirī al-masjid al-ḥarām): Refers to residents within the miqat of Makkah, considered as residing near the Sacred Mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding a person from Makkah performing Qiran?
A) Valid, with a Hadi
B) Valid, without a Hadi
C) Invalid, only ifrad allowed
D) Makruh but valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts tamattu' and qiran to non-residents of Makkah based on the Quranic condition in verse 2:96.

Returning Home Invalidates Tamattu'
Ruling on tamattu' becoming void if the pilgrim returns home after Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid tamattu' and apply the ruling when a pilgrim returns home after Umrah.

Core Idea
Returning home between Umrah and Hajj breaks the single journey condition and invalidates tamattu'.

Tamattu' is a special form of Hajj where you perform Umrah and then Hajj in the same year, without returning home. However, what if you go home after Umrah? This lesson examines a key condition: the journey must be continuous. We will explore the ruling and its evidence from the athar of Ata'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify that the act under discussion is tamattu', and the ruling is that returning home after Umrah without a hadi invalidates it.
2
Locate the condition
Recognize the underlying condition: tamattu' requires a single continuous journey. Returning home breaks this unity.
3
Examine the evidence
Analyze the athar from Ata' that states: 'Whoever performs Umrah in the months of Hajj then returns to his country, then performs Hajj in the same year, he is not a mutamatti'.' This is the proof.
4
Distinguish with Hadi
Note the exception: if the pilgrim had brought a Hadi (sacrificial animal) which necessitates returning to Makkah, then the journey is considered continuous and tamattu' remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا عاد المتمتع الى بلده بعد فراغه من العمرة ولم يكن ساق الهدى بطل تمتعه [ ۷۰۸] (۱۴) اگر تمتع کرنے والا عمرہ سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد اپنے شہر آجائے اور ہدی نہ ہانکی ہو تو اس کا تمتع باطل ہو جائے گا۔ (1) ہری نہ ہانکی ہو تو اپنے اہل وعیال کے ساتھ ملنے اور اپنے شہر جانے سے پہلا سفر باطل ہو گیا۔ شہر کے ساتھ المسام صحیح ہو گیا۔ اور ایک سفر میں عمرہ اور حج ادا نہ کیا تو تمتع اور قرآن نہ ہوئے اس لئے تمتع باطل ہو گیا (۲) اثر میں ہے . عن عطاء قال من اعتمر في شهر الحج ثم رجع الى بلده ثم حج من عامه فليس بمتمتع، انما المتمتع من اقام ولم يرجع (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی هیتة، ۴۷ فی الرجل يعتمر في اشہر الحج ثم رجع ثم سیج ، ج ثالث ص ۵۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۰۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ کر کے گھر چلا گیا تو تمتع فاسد ہو گیا۔ اگر ہدی ساتھ لایا تھا اور پھر عمرہ کر کے گھر چلا گیا تو ہری کی وجہ سے مکہ مکرمہ میں واپس آنا ضروری ہے اس لئے پہلا سفر باطل نہیں ہوا اور گھر کے ساتھ الہام صحیح نہیں ہوا اس لئے جمتع باطل نہیں ہوگا۔
And if the mutamatti' returns to his country after completing Umrah and he had not brought the Hadi, his tamattu' becomes invalid. [708] If the person performing tamattu' returns to his city after completing Umrah and had not taken a Hadi, then his tamattu' becomes void. (1) If he had not taken a Hadi, then by meeting his family and going to his city, the first journey becomes void. The connection with the city becomes correct. And he did not perform Umrah and Hajj in one journey, so it is not tamattu' or qiran, hence tamattu' becomes void. (2) There is an athar from Ata: 'Whoever performs Umrah in the months of Hajj then returns to his country, then performs Hajj in the same year, he is not a mutamatti'. The mutamatti' is the one who stays and does not return.' From this athar, it is understood that if he went home after Umrah, tamattu' becomes invalid. If he had brought a Hadi and returned home after Umrah, then due to the Hadi, it is necessary to return to Makkah, so the first journey is not void and the bond with the city is not correct, so tamattu' does not become invalid.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This is a ruling concerning the validity of tamattu' when the pilgrim returns to his homeland after the Umrah portion. The key condition for tamattu' is that Umrah and Hajj are performed in a single journey, without an intervening return home. If the person returns home without having brought a Hadi (which would necessitate returning to Makkah), then the unity of the journey is broken and tamattu' becomes invalid (fāsid). However, if the person brought a Hadi (a sacrificial animal) that requires him to return to Makkah, then the journey is considered continuous and tamattu' remains valid. The athar from Ata' confirms this: tamattu' is only valid for one who stays in Makkah after Umrah until Hajj.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj performed by first doing Umrah in the months of Hajj, then becoming halal, then performing Hajj later in the same year, all in one journey.
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal brought by the pilgrim for tamattu' or qiran.
أثر (athar): A narration from a Companion or a Tabi'i, not directly from the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to tamattu' if a person returns to his home after Umrah without having brought a Hadi?
A) It is still valid
B) It becomes invalid
C) He must give a Hadi to restore it
D) He must fast three days

Key Takeaway
The validity of tamattu' depends on a continuous journey; returning home without a hadi invalidates it.

Majority of Tawaf Circuits and Tamattu' Status
Ruling on when Umrah performed before Hajj months affects tamattu' status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of 'majority considered as the whole' to determine tamattu' status based on the number of tawaf circuits performed before the months of Hajj.

Core Idea
The majority of tawaf circuits performed before Hajj months decides tamattu' status.

In Hajj, a person performing Umrah and then Hajj in the same journey may be a mutamatti', which requires Umrah to be performed during the months of Hajj. This lesson clarifies a key nuance: when Umrah begins before the months but is completed during them, the number of tawaf circuits completed before the months determines whether the Umrah counts as being in Hajj months. The Hanafi rely on a usul principle that the majority of an action is legally equivalent to the whole.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person begins Umrah before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first 10 of Dhul Hijjah) and performs some tawaf circuits before the months start.
The determination hinges on the number of circuits completed before the months begin.
2
Count the circuits performed before Hajj months
Out of the seven circuits of Umrah tawaf, count how many were completed before the first day of Shawwal (or before the months start).
3
Apply the majority rule
If the number is less than 4 (the majority of 7), then the Umrah is considered to have occurred during Hajj months, and the person becomes mutamatti'. If 4 or more circuits were done before the months, the Umrah is considered pre-Hajj, and the person is not mutamatti'.
The Hanafi principle: 'the majority of an act is like the whole' (akthar ka al-kull).
4
Understand the usul basis
This ruling derives from the usul al-fiqh principle that when an act is composed of parts, the majority stands in place of the entire act for legal purposes.
This is a Hanafi-specific application; other schools may differ.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require the entire tawaf to be performed within the Hajj months for the Umrah to count as being during the months.
The Hanafi position is based on ease and the principle of majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن احرم بالعمرة قبل اشهر الحج فطاف لها اقل من اربعة اشواط ثم دخلت اشهر الحج فتممها واحرم بالحج كان متمتعا فان طاف لها اربعة اشواط فصاعدا ثم احرم بالحج من عامه فليس بمتمتع [ ۷۰۹] (۱۵) جس نے حج کے مہینے سے پہلے عمرے کا احرام باندھا اور چار شوط سے کم طواف کیا پھر حج کا مہینہ داخل ہوا اور عمرہ کو پورا کیا اور حج کا احرام باندھا تو تمتع کرنے والا ہو گا۔ اور اگر حج کے مہینے سے پہلے عمرے کا طواف چار شوط کیا یا اس سے زیادہ کیا پھر اسی سال حج کیا تو یہ تمتع کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا۔ تمتع ہونے کے لئے دو شرطیں ہیں، ایک یہ کہ حج سے پہلے عمرہ کیا ہو، اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ عمرہ حج کے مہینے میں ادا کیا ہو۔ حج کا مہینہ پہلی شوال سے دس ذی الحجہ تک ہے۔ دوسر آسول یہ ہے کہ اکثر شوط کا اعتبار ہے تو سات میں اکثر شوط چار ہیں اور اقل شوط تین ہیں۔
And whoever enters ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj and performs less than four circuits (ashwat) of tawaf, then the months of Hajj enter and he completes it and enters ihram for Hajj, he is a mutamatti'. If he performed four circuits or more, then he enters ihram for Hajj in the same year, he is not a mutamatti'. [709] The one who tied ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj and performed less than four circuits, then the month of Hajj entered and he completed Umrah and tied ihram for Hajj, then he will be a mutamatti'. And if he performed four circuits of tawaf for Umrah before the months of Hajj or more, then performed Hajj in the same year, he will not be a mutamatti'. For tamattu', there are two conditions: one, that Umrah is performed before Hajj, and the second condition is that Umrah is performed in the months of Hajj. The months of Hajj are from 1st Shawwal to 10th Dhul Hijjah. Another principle: consideration is given to the majority of circuits; then in seven, the majority is four, and the minimum is three.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This ruling determines when a person becomes a mutamatti'. The key factor is whether a substantial part of Umrah (majority of tawaf) was performed before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first 10 of Dhul Hijjah). The Hanafi principle used here is that the majority (akthar) of an action is considered equivalent to the whole in legal ruling (a usul al-fiqh principle). Since Umrah tawaf consists of seven circuits, the majority is four. If a person performs less than four circuits before the Hajj months start, then when he completes Umrah and performs Hajj in the same journey, he is a mutamatti'. If he performed four or more circuits before the months, the Umrah is considered to have been performed before Hajj months, so he is not considered a mutamatti' (instead it is considered as if he performed Umrah before the months, and then Hajj separately). This distinction affects the obligation of dam (sacrificial animal) for tamattu'.

Key Terms
اشہر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah.
اکثر شوط (akthar shawṭ): The majority of circuits; in a seven-circuit tawaf, the majority is four.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs 3 circuits of tawaf for Umrah before Shawwal, then completes the remaining circuits in Shawwal, then performs Hajj, what is his status?
A) Mutamatti'
B) Not mutamatti'
C) Qarin
D) Mufrid

Key Takeaway
Umrah performed before Hajj months results in tamattu' only if less than the majority of tawaf circuits (4 out of 7) were completed before the months begin.

Rulings on Types of Hajj and the Months of Hajj
Rulings on Ifrad, Tamattu', Qiran, and timing with proofs from Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the three types of Hajj for Makkans and non-Makkans, explain the conditions for a valid tamattu', and apply the definition of the months of Hajj to determine the validity of tamattu'.

Core Idea
Makkans only Ifrad; non-Makkans may do Tamattu' or Qiran with hady, subject to strict timing and residence conditions.

This passage from Al Sharh al-Thamari presents the Hanafi rulings on the types of Hajj, distinguishing between residents of Makkah (and those within the miqat) and others. It also defines the months of Hajj and provides conditions for tamattu' based on the number of tawaf performed before the months. We will examine the proofs, conditions, and cross-madhhab disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for each group
The passage begins by stating that for the people of Makkah, only Ifrad is permissible; for others, Tamattu' and Qiran are allowed with the obligation of hady.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Hanafi proof is the Quranic verse (2:196) and its interpretation by Ibn Abbas, which is cited in the text.
The phrase 'that is for those whose family are not present at the Sacred Mosque' is the key.
3
Analyze the conditions for a valid tamattu'
The passage details several conditions: Umrah must be in the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first ten of Dhul Hijjah), before Hajj, and the majority of tawaf (four or more circuits) must be performed within those months. Additionally, returning home after Umrah without a hady animal invalidates tamattu'.
The majority rule is based on the principle that most of the tawaf determines when the Umrah is considered performed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with other schools
Imam al-Shafi'i interprets the verse as referring to the obligation of hady, not restricting the type of Hajj, so he permits tamattu' for all without hady. Imam Malik holds that hady is not required for Makkans.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that a Makkan cannot perform tamattu' in the Hanafi school, but can in the Shafi'i school.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Use the conditions to determine whether a given sequence of Umrah and Hajj constitutes valid tamattu'.
For example, if three tawaf are performed before Shawwal, the Umrah is not in the months, so tamattu' fails.

كتاب الحج انما لهم الافراد خاصة تفسیر ہے کہ اہل مکہ کے علاوہ کے لئے تمتع اور قرآن ہے۔ عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن متعة الحج ... وابا حه للناس غير اهل مكة قال الله تعالى ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام (بخاری شریف ، باب قول الله تعالی ذلک لمن لم یکن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۵۷۲/ مصنف ابن ابی هیسته ۱۸۱ من کان لا یری علی اہل مکتہ محعه ، ج ثالث ، ص ۴۱۶، نمبر ۱۵۶۹۰) انده امام شافعی کے نزدیک آیت میں ذلک کا اشارہ تمتع نہیں ہے بلکہ ہدی ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک کی تمتع اور قران تو کر سکتا ہے البتہ اس پر ہدی لازم نہیں ہے۔ قال يحيى سئل مالك عن رجل ... وانما الهدى او الصيام على من لم يكن من اهل مكة (الف) (موطا امام مالك ما جاء فی التمتع ص ۳۵۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ یکی پر ہدی اور روزہ نہیں ہے۔
[۷۰۸ (۱۴) اگر تمتع کرنے والا عمرہ سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد اپنے شہر آجائے اور ہدی نہ ہانکی ہو تو اس کا تمتع باطل ہو جائے گا۔ (1) ہری نہ ہانکی ہو تو اپنے اہل وعیال کے ساتھ ملنے اور اپنے شہر جانے سے پہلا سفر باطل ہو گیا۔ شہر کے ساتھ المسام صحیح ہو گیا۔ اور ایک سفر میں عمرہ اور حج ادا نہ کیا تو تمتع اور قرآن نہ ہوئے اس لئے تمتع باطل ہو گیا (۲) اثر میں ہے . عن عطاء قال من اعتمر في شهر الحج ثم رجع الى بلده ثم حج من عامه فليس بمتمتع، انما المتمتع من اقام ولم يرجع (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی هیتة ، ۴۷ فی الرجل يعتمر في اشہر الحج ثم رجع ثم سیج ، ج ثالث ص ۵۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۰۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ کر کے گھر چلا گیا تو تمتع فاسد ہو گیا۔ اگر ہدی ساتھ لایا تھا اور پھر عمرہ کر کے گھر چلا گیا تو ہری کی وجہ سے مکہ مکرمہ میں واپس آنا ضروری ہے اس لئے پہلا سفر باطل نہیں ہوا اور گھر کے ساتھ الہام صحیح نہیں ہوا اس لئے جمتع باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ [۷۰۹] (۱۵) جس نے حج کے مہینے سے پہلے عمرے کا احرام باندھا اور چار شوط سے کم طواف کیا پھر حج کا مہینہ داخل ہوا اور عمرہ کو پورا کیا ارحج کا احرام باندھا تو تمتع کرنے والا ہو گا۔ اور اگر حج کے مہینے سے پہلے عمرے کا طواف چار شوط کیا یا اس سے زیادہ کیا پھر اسی سال حج کیا تو یہ تمتع کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا۔ تمتع ہونے کے لئے دو شرطیں ہیں، ایک یہ کہ حج سے پہلے عمرہ کیا ہو، اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ عمرہ حج کے مہینے میں ادا کیا ہو۔ حج کا مہینہ پہلی شوال سے دس ذی الحجہ تک ہے۔ دوسر آسول یہ ہے کہ اکثر شوط کا اعتبار ہے تو سات میں اکثر شوط چار ہیں اور اقل شوط تین ہیں۔ پس اگر حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت میں سے ایک آدمی کے بارے میں پوچھا گیا۔ فرمایا ہدی یا روزہ اس پر ہے جو اہل مکہ میں سے نہ ہو یعنی میقات کے اندر میں سے نہ ہو (ب) حضرت امام مطا نے فرمایا جس نے شوال، ذی قعد و یا ذی الحجہ میں عمرہ کیا پھر اپنے اہل کی طرف لوٹا پھر اسی سال حج کیا تو اس پر ہی نہیں ہے۔ ہندی اس پر ہے جس نے اشہر حج میں عمرہ کیا پھر مکہ میں حج تک ٹھہرا رہا پھر حج کیا۔
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل) ۴۳۴ كتاب الحج لعمرته قبل اشهر الحج اربعة اشواط فصاعدا ثم حج من عامه ذلك لم يكن متمتعا [۱۰](۱۶) واشهر الحج شوال و ذو القعدة وعشر من ذى الحجة [۱۱] (۱) فان اکثر شوط یعنی عمرے Book of Hajj. Only Ifrad is for them (the people of Makkah). Explanation: For the people of Makkah, only Ifrad; for others, Tamattu' and Qiran. From Ibn Abbas that he was asked about mut'ah of Hajj... and he permitted it for non-Makkans, reciting the verse 'That is for those whose family are not present at the Sacred Mosque' (Sahih Bukhari...). According to Imam Shafi'i, the verse refers to the hady, not Tamattu', so he permits Tamattu' and Qiran without obligatory hady. Yahya said: Malik was asked about a man... and the hady or fasting is only for those not from the people of Makkah (Muwatta). From this athar it is understood that hady and fasting are not required for the people of Makkah.
[708] (14) If the mutamatti' returns to his country after completing Umrah and he did not bring the hady, his tamattu' becomes invalid. Explanation: If the hady was not brought, the first journey (for Umrah) becomes invalid because he joined his family and returned to his city. The connection (with the sacred precincts) is lost, and since he did not perform Hajj in the same journey, tamattu' is invalid. There is an athar from 'Ata: Whoever performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and then returns to his country, then performs Hajj in that year, he is not mutamatti'; the mutamatti' is one who stays (in Makkah). From this athar it is learned that performing Umrah and returning home invalidates tamattu'. If he brought the hady and then performed Umrah and returned home, he must return to Makkah due to the hady, so the first journey remains valid and tamattu' is valid.
[709] (15) Whoever enters ihram for Umrah before the months of Hajj and performs less than four tawaf, then the months of Hajj enter and he completes the Umrah and enters ihram for Hajj, he is mutamatti'. If he performed four or more tawaf for his Umrah before the months, then he performed Hajj in the same year, he is not mutamatti'. There are two conditions for tamattu': first, Umrah before Hajj; second, Umrah performed during the months of Hajj. The months of Hajj are from the first of Shawwal to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The principle: the majority of tawaf is considered; in seven tawaf, the majority is four, and the minimum is three.
Margin notes: (a) He was asked about a man... He said: Hady or fasting is on the one who is not from the people of Makkah, i.e., not from within the miqat. (b) Imam Malik said: Whoever performs Umrah in Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, or Dhul Hijjah, then returns to his family, then performs Hajj in the same year, there is no hady on him. Hady is on the one who performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and stays in Makkah until Hajj.
(On page 439) Al Sharh al-Thamari, part one, page 434, Book of Hajj. For his Umrah before the months of Hajj, four or more tawaf, then he performs Hajj in that same year, he is not mutamatti'. [710] (16) The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and ten days from Dhul Hijjah. [711] (1) So if the majority of tawaf (i.e., four) is performed before Shawwal, then tamattu' is not valid because Umrah was performed before the months. If the majority is performed in Shawwal, then tamattu' is valid. From Abdullah ibn Umar: Whoever performs Umrah in the months of Hajj in Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, or Dhul Hijjah before Hajj, then stays in Makkah until Hajj, he is mutamatti' and must offer what is easy of hady. From Ibn Abbas: The months of Hajj mentioned in Allah's book are Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and Dhul Hijjah; whoever performs tamattu' in these months, upon him is a dam. From these two athars, the conditions are derived: Umrah in the Hajj months and before Hajj. If Umrah is performed after Hajj, it is not tamattu' and no dam is obligatory. Definition of a tawaf: one circuit around the Kaaba. [711] (17) If one enters ihram for Hajj before these months, his Hajj is valid. If he enters ihram for Hajj before Shawwal, e.g., in Ramadan, the ihram is valid and Hajj is correct. Ihram is a condition for Hajj, and a condition can be performed beforehand, just as wudu can be performed before the prayer time. However, entering ihram so early is makruh. Commentary
This passage from Al Sharh al-Thamari covers several key rulings in the Book of Hajj. It begins by stating the Hanafi position that the people of Makkah (and those within the miqat) are restricted to Ifrad (Hajj alone without Umrah). This is based on the Quranic verse (2:196) and the hadith of Ibn Abbas. The passage then notes the disagreement with Imam Shafi'i, who interprets the verse as referring to the obligation of hady, not the type of Hajj, and with Imam Malik, who holds that hady is not required for those from Makkah. The Hanafi position is that for non-Makkans, Tamattu' and Qiran are permissible with the obligation of hady. The text then addresses specific cases: (14) If a mutamatti' performs Umrah and returns home without bringing a sacrificial animal, his tamattu' becomes invalid because the unity of the journey is broken. This is supported by an athar from 'Ata. However, if he brought the animal, he must return to Makkah for it, so the tamattu' remains valid. (15) details the conditions for a valid tamattu': Umrah must be performed during the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first ten of Dhul Hijjah) and before Hajj. A crucial point is that if the majority of the tawaf (four or more circuits) is performed before the months of Hajj, the Umrah is considered to have taken place before the months, and thus tamattu' is not achieved. The text also defines the months of Hajj, citing Quranic verses and the interpretation of Ibn Abbas. Finally, (17) explains that ihram for Hajj can be entered before the months, and the Hajj will be valid, though it is makruh to do so. The analogy with wudu before prayer time is used to justify the validity. Overall, the passage provides a comprehensive treatment of the rules governing the types of Hajj and their timing, with evidence from primary sources.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah during the months of Hajj, then performing Hajj in the same year, with a hady obligation.
قران (qiran): Performing both Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram.
افراد (ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without Umrah.
شوط (shawt): One complete circuit around the Kaaba in tawaf.
اشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs Umrah in Shawwal, performs 3 tawaf, then enters ihram for Hajj after completing Umrah, is this tamattu'?
A) Yes, because Umrah was in the months of Hajj
B) Yes, because he completed Umrah before Hajj
C) No, because he performed less than four tawaf before the months
D) No, because he needs to perform four tawaf to be mutamatti'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts Tamattu' and Qiran to non-Makkans only, with strict conditions on the timing of Umrah tawaf and the pilgrim's stay in Makkah.

beginner
6 min
Months of Hajj and Condition for Tamattu'
Defines months of Hajj and tamattu' condition via hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the months of Hajj and explain the condition for tamattu' using the Hanafi position, including the majority-of-circuits rule.

Core Idea
Tamattu' requires 'Umrah during the months of Hajj; the majority of tawaf circuits determine the timing.

This passage defines the months of Hajj and establishes a key condition for tamattu' – that the 'Umrah must be performed within those months. The author uses a hadith from Ibn 'Umar to clarify that performing the majority of tawaf circuits suffices. Understanding this condition is essential for determining when a sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and condition
Read the first part of the passage: tamattu' is valid only if 'Umrah is performed in the months of Hajj. Note the specific condition: the majority of tawaf circuits must be in those months.
The text uses 'four circuits' as the majority threshold for a tawaf of seven circuits.
2
Locate the months of Hajj
Find the explicit list: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. This is based on the interpretation of 'ashhur ma'lumat' in the Quran and the hadith.
The author cites Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar as authorities.
3
Understand the majority rule
The text states: if the majority of circuits (four or more) are performed in the months of Hajj, the 'Umrah counts as being in those months, even if some circuits fall outside.
This is a practical Hanafi rule to resolve timing ambiguities.
4
Examine the proof
The hadith from Ibn 'Umar explicitly says: 'Whoever performs 'Umrah in the months of Hajj...before Hajj...then he is a mutamatti'.' This is the primary dalil.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but accepted in practice.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario where a person performs 4 circuits of 'Umrah in Shawwal and 3 in Dhu al-Qa'dah, then performs Hajj, determine that they are a mutamatti' because the majority of circuits were in the months.
This illustrates the practical application of the rule.

امام مالک، باب ماجاء فی التمتع ص ۳۵۵ / مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، نمبر ۱۳۰۰۰) عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن متعة الحج فقال ... اشهر الحج التي ذكر الله تعالى في كتابه شوال و ذو القعدة وذو الحجة فمن تمتع فى هذه الاشهر فعليه دم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب قول الله عز وجل ذلك لمن لم یکن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) اس دونوں اثر سے شرطوں کا پتہ چلا ، ایک یہ کہ حج کے مہینہ میں عمرہ کیا ہو اور دوسرا یہ کہ حج سے پہلے کیا ہو تب تمتع ہو گا۔ اور اگر حج کے بعد عمرہ کیا تو تمتع نہیں ہوگا اور نہ اس پر دم تمتع لازم ہوگا۔ اخت شوط : بیت اللہ کے گرد ایک چکر لگا کر ایک طواف کرنے کو ایک شوط کہتے ہیں۔ [۷۰۱](۱۶) حج کا مہینہ شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ تک ہے۔ اس کی وجہ مسئلہ نمبر ۱۵ میں حدیث گزرگئی (۲) آیت میں ہے الحج اشهر معلومات فمن فرض فيهن الحج فلا رفت ولا فسوق ولا جدال في الحج (ج) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورة البقرة ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ حج کے کچھ مہینے معلوم ہیں جس میں حج کا احرام باندھے۔ اور عبد اللہ بن عباس کی تفسیر یہ ہے کہ وہ مہینے شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ ہیں۔ جیسا کہ مسلہ نمبر۱۵ میں گزرا ( بخاری شریف، باب قول الله عز وجل ذلك لمن لم یکن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۵۷۲ رسنن سبیھقی، باب بیان اشهر الحج ج رابع ص ۵۵۹ نمبر ۸۷۱۱) اس سے معلوم ہو کہ حج کے مہینے شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ کی دس تاریخ تک ہیں۔ سن بیہقی میں دس ذی الحجہ تک کی تصریح موجود ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ جس نے اشہر حج شوال، ذی قعدہ بازی الحجہ میں عمرہ کیا حج سے پہلے پھر مکہ مکرمہ میں ٹھہرا رہا یہاں تک کہ اس کو حج نے پالیا تو وہ جمع کرنے والا ہے۔ اگر جج کیا اور اس پر جو آسان ہو وہ ہدی لازم ہے (ب) تمتع کے بارے میں حضرت ابن عباس سے پوچھا اشہر حج وہ ہیں جن کو اللہ نے اپنی کتاب میں ذکر کیا شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ تو جس نے ان مہینوں میں تمتع کیا تو اس پر دم ہے (ج) حج کے مہینے معلوم ہیں۔ پس جس نے ان میں حج فرض کیا تو جماع کی اور فسق کی باتیں نہ کریں اور نہ حج میں جھگڑا ہے۔
Book of Hajj. If he performs more than four circuits of his 'Umrah before the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in that same year, he is not a mutamatti'. And the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah. If the majority of circuits, meaning four circuits of 'Umrah, are performed before Shawwal, then tamattu' does not occur, because the 'Umrah was performed before the months of Hajj. And if the majority of circuits, meaning four circuits, are performed in Shawwal, then since the 'Umrah was performed in the month of Hajj, tamattu' occurs...
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hajj and presents a ruling on tamattu'. The matn states that if one performs more than half of the tawaf of 'Umrah (i.e., four circuits) before the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year, he is not a mutamatti'. The Urdu commentary explains that the condition for tamattu' is that the 'Umrah must be performed within the months of Hajj. Two athar are cited: from Ibn 'Umar and Ibn 'Abbas, establishing that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah, and that tamattu' requires 'Umrah in these months before Hajj. The passage also defines 'shaut' as one circuit around the Ka'bah. The commentary concludes with a verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:197) and its interpretation by Ibn 'Abbas.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The specific months for Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
تمتع (tamattu'): A form of Hajj where one first performs 'Umrah in the months of Hajj, then performs Hajj in the same year, with a sacrifice due.
شوط (shawt): One complete circuit around the Ka'bah in tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs four circuits of 'Umrah tawaf in Shawwal and the remaining three in Dhu al-Qa'dah, then performs Hajj, is he a mutamatti'?
A) Yes, because the majority of circuits were in the months of Hajj.
B) No, because the 'Umrah was not completed entirely in the months.
C) Yes, as long as any part of 'Umrah is in the months.
D) No, because tamattu' requires all circuits in the months.

Key Takeaway
The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah; tamattu' requires 'Umrah within these months before Hajj, with the majority of tawaf circuits determining the timing.

Ihram for Hajj Before the Months
States ruling and Shafi'i disagreement on ihram before Hajj months.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihram before Hajj months and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, citing the evidence from the two athars.

Core Idea
Ihram for Hajj before the months is valid but makruh; it does not become 'Umrah as Shafi'is hold.

The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. But what if someone enters ihram earlier, say in Ramadan? Is the Hajj valid? The Hanafi school says yes, though disliked. The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that it converts to 'Umrah. In this lesson, we examine the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules: ihram before the months is valid for Hajj but makruh (disliked).
Makruh here is likely makruh tahrimi because it contradicts the Sunnah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such ihram is not valid for Hajj but automatically becomes 'Umrah.
This is a direct consequence of a different interpretation of the evidence.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school relies on the athar of Ibn 'Abbas: 'That is not from the Sunnah.' This indicates the act is not part of the established practice, implying karahah but not invalidation.
The athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, transmitted as a single narration (zanni al-thubut).
4
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school uses the athar of 'Ata': 'Whoever performs ihram for Hajj outside the months should make it an 'Umrah.' This is taken as a command to convert.
The 'Ata' athar is also from al-Bayhaqi and is zanni in transmission.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says the person has a valid Hajj (though sinful for early ihram); Shafi'i says the Hajj is invalid and he must still perform Hajj later. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the first view.
Knowing this prevents confusion when applying the ruling in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدم الاحرام بالحج عليها جاز احرامه وانعقد حجه (1) پس اگر حج کا احرام ان مہینوں سے پہلے باندھا تو اس کا حج منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ حج کے مہینے سے پہلے یعنی شوال سے پہلے رمضان ہی میں حج کا احرام باندھ لیا تو احرام منعقد ہو جائے گا اور حج کرنا صحیح ہوگا۔ (۱) احرام حج کے لئے شرط کے درجہ میں ہے اور شرط مقدم ہو جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ جیسے وضو نماز کے وقت سے پہلے کر سکتا ہے اسی طرح حج کا احرام حج کے مہینے سے پہلے باندھے تو باند سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اتنا پہلے احرام باندھنا مکروہ ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس في الرجل يــحــم بالحج في غير اشهر الحج قال ليس ذلك من السنة (الف) (سن للبیھقی، باب لا يصل بالج في غير اشهر الحج ج رابع ص ۱۵۶۱، نمبر ۸۷۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اشھر حج سے پہلے حج کا احرام باندھے تو وہ سنت کے خلاف ہے یعنی مکروہ ہے۔ تاہم حج کا احترام ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اشہر حج سے پہلے احرام باندھا تو حج نہیں ہوگا وہ عمرہ کے احترام میں تبدیل ہو جائے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یا اثر ہے عن عطاء قال من احرم بالحج في غير اشهر الحج جعلها عمرة (ب) ( سنن سيحقی، باب لا يصل بالج فی غیر اشهر الحج ج رابع ص ۱۵۶۱، نمبر ۸۷۲۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اشہر حج کے علاوہ میں حج کا احرام باندھے تو اس کو عمرہ بنادے (۲) اوپر کا عبد اللہ بن عباس کا اثر بھی امام شافعی کی دلیل ہے۔
If he advances the ihram for Hajj before it (the months), his ihram is permissible and his Hajj is valid. Then the Urdu: So if he ties ihram for Hajj before these months, his Hajj will be concluded. If he ties ihram for Hajj before the month of Hajj, i.e., in Ramadan, then the ihram is concluded and performing Hajj is valid. (1) Ihram for Hajj is like a condition, and a condition can be advanced... However, tying ihram this early is makruh. (2) From Ibn 'Abbas regarding a man who performs ihram for Hajj outside the months of Hajj, he said: That is not from the Sunnah. This athar shows that tying ihram before the months of Hajj is against the Sunnah, i.e., makruh. Nevertheless, his Hajj is valid. Imam Shafi'i says that if he ties ihram before the months, his Hajj will not be valid and it will convert to 'Umrah. Their evidence is the athar from 'Ata': 'Whoever performs ihram for Hajj outside the months of Hajj, he should make it an 'Umrah.' So this athar shows that if he ties ihram for Hajj outside the months, he should make it an 'Umrah.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i. The Hanafi position is that ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, Dhu al-Hijjah) is valid, and the Hajj is concluded. However, it is makruh because it goes against the Sunnah, as evidenced by the athar of Ibn 'Abbas. The Shafi'i position, based on an athar from 'Ata', is that such ihram is not valid for Hajj and automatically becomes 'Umrah. The Hanafi commentary clarifies that the athar of Ibn 'Abbas supports the Hanafi view of validity with karahah, while the Shafi'i use the athar of 'Ata' to argue conversion. The passage does not provide a Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence beyond the earlier athar.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah, entered by intention and reciting talbiyah.
مكروه (makruh): An act that is disliked but not sinful; here, tying ihram before the months is makruh (likely makruh tahrimi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs ihram for Hajj in Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) The ihram is invalid and becomes 'Umrah.
B) The ihram is valid for Hajj but it is makruh.
C) The ihram is valid and recommended.
D) The ihram is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Ihram for Hajj before the months is valid but makruh; it does not become 'Umrah, contrary to the Shafi'i view.

Ruling on the Menstruating Woman Performing Hajj Rites
Ruling on menstruating woman at ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a menstruating woman at the time of ihram and apply it by identifying which rites are deferred.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman performs all Hajj rites except tawaf until she purifies.

Many assume a woman in menses cannot perform Hajj, but Islamic law provides a clear exception. This passage clarifies that she may complete all the rituals except circumambulation of the Ka'bah (tawaf), which is deferred until she becomes pure. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary hardship and ensures that the obligation of Hajj is fulfilled correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the general rule
Read the matn: when a woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she should perform ghusl, enter ihram, and do as the pilgrim does. Highlight the default: all rites are obligatory for her.
The act of ihram itself is not prevented.
2
Isolate the exception
Note the phrase 'except that she does not perform tawaf around the House until she becomes pure.' This is the sole exclusion. Understand that tawaf requires ritual purity (taharah) which is absent during menstruation.
The exception is temporary; tawaf must be made up later.
3
Understand the rationale
The Urdu commentary explains that other rites occur in open areas outside the Sacred Mosque, whereas tawaf requires entering the mosque, which is forbidden for a menstruating woman. This difference in location is the underlying reason.
Fiqh principle: darar (harm) is removed, but essential acts are not dropped.
4
Examine the dalil (proof)
The hadith of 'A'ishah is cited: the Prophet instructed her to do everything the pilgrims do except tawaf until she purifies. This hadith is the explicit textual evidence for the ruling.
The hadith also applies to nifas (post‑natal bleeding).
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Imagine a woman who begins her period on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. She performs ghusl, dons ihram, proceeds to Arafat, Muzdalifah, and Mina for stoning and sacrifice. She delays tawaf and sa'y until her period ends after the 10th.
She must not perform tawaf or sa'y (if she intends sa'y) until pure, but she can do all other rites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا حاضت المرأة عند الاحرام اغتسلت واحرمت وصنعت كما يصنع الحاج غير انها لا تطوف بالبيت حتى تظهر [۱۲](۱۸) إذا كانت المرأة حائضًا في وقت الإحرام، فإنها تغتسل وتحرم وتصنع ما يصنع الحاج، إلا أنها لا تطوف بالبيت حتى تطهر. (۱) توضیحات: اگر عورت احرام کے وقت حائضہ ہو جائے تو غسل کرے اور احرام باندھے اور وہی اعمال کرے جو حاجی کرتے ہیں، علاوہ یہ کہ بیت اللہ کا طواف نہ کرے جب تک کہ پاک نہ ہو جائے۔ طواف کے علاوہ حج کے تمام کام صحرا میں ہوتے ہیں اس لئے حائضہ عورت وہ کر سکتی ہے البتہ طواف مسجد حرام میں ہوتا ہے اور حائضہ مسجد میں داخل نہیں ہو سکتی اس لئے طواف نہیں کرے گی۔ اور باقی حج کے تمام کام کرے گی (۲) حدیث میں بھی اس کا ثبوت ہے عن عائشة صلی الله عليها قالت خرجنا مع النبي عل... فقال انفست يعنى الحيضة قالت قلت نعم قال ان هذه شيء كتبه الله على بنات آدم فاقضي ما يقضى الحج غير ان لا تطوفى بالبيت حتی تغتسلی قالت و ضحی رسول الله نسائه بالبقرة (ج)(مسلم شریف، باب بیان وجوه الاحرام وانه یجوز افراد الحج والتمتع والقران ص ۳۸۸ نمبر ۲۹۱۸/۱۲۱۱ / بخاری شریف، باب کیف نقل الحائض والنفساء ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۵۵۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حائضہ اور نفساء عورت حج کا احرام باندھے گی البتہ طواف نہیں کرے گی۔
And if a woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs ghusl and enters ihram and does as the pilgrim does, except that she does not perform tawaf around the House until she becomes pure. (12)(18) Clarification: If a woman becomes menstruating at the time of ihram, she should perform ghusl and tie ihram and perform the same actions that the pilgrim performs, except that she should not perform tawaf of the Ka'bah until she becomes pure. Because all other rites of Hajj are performed in the desert, so a menstruating woman can do them; however, tawaf is in the Masjid al-Haram and a menstruating woman cannot enter the mosque, so she will not perform tawaf. And she will perform the rest of the Hajj actions. (2) There is proof in the hadith from 'A'ishah: She said, 'We went out with the Prophet... he said: Have you menstruated? She said: Yes. He said: This is a thing that Allah has decreed upon the daughters of Adam. So perform what the pilgrim performs, except do not perform tawaf around the House until you purify yourself.' She said: And the Prophet sacrificed a cow for his wives.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a woman who menstruates at the time of ihram. The Arabic matn says she should perform ghusl, enter ihram, and do all the acts of Hajj except tawaf until she becomes pure (طهر). The Urdu commentary explains that all other rites occur in open areas (like Arafat, Muzdalifah, Mina), so they are permissible for a menstruating woman, but tawaf requires entering the mosque, which is prohibited for a menstruating woman. The hadith of 'A'ishah is cited as proof, where the Prophet instructed her to do everything the pilgrims do except tawaf until she purifies. This hadith also applies to a woman in nifas (postnatal bleeding). The ruling is clear: the obligation of Hajj is not waived, but tawaf is deferred.

Key Terms
حائض (ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah, a pillar (rukn) of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman menstruates just before entering ihram for Hajj. What should she do?
A) She cannot perform Hajj at all.
B) She should delay ihram until she is pure.
C) She should perform ghusl, enter ihram, and do all rites except tawaf.
D) She should enter ihram but skip all rites until pure.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman performs all Hajj rites except tawaf, which she must perform after purification.

Menstruation After Wuquf and Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Ruling on Tawaf al-Wada' Waiver
Ruling on a menstruating woman after completing the essential Hajj rites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a menstruating woman who has completed Tawaf al-Ziyarah and determine whether Tawaf al-Wada' is required.

Core Idea
If a woman menstruates after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, she may leave without Tawaf al-Wada' — no penalty.

This lesson addresses a specific concession in Hajj for women. The matn states a brief ruling, and the commentary clarifies that when a woman menstruates after completing the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the remaining wajib of Tawaf al-Wada' is waived. No fidyah is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Timing
The ruling applies only when menstruation occurs after both Wuquf at 'Arafah and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If it occurs before these, a different ruling applies.
Tawaf al-Wada' is normally wajib for all pilgrims leaving Mecca.
2
State the Consequence: She Departs
The text says 'she departs' (انصرفت), meaning she may leave Mecca without performing Tawaf al-Wada'.
This is a dispensation (rukhsah) for menstruating women.
3
Determine the Legal Effect: No Compensation
No dam (sacrifice) or fidyah is required because the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah has been performed, and the wajib is waived due to a valid excuse.
Normally, missing Tawaf al-Wada' requires a dam; here it is dropped.
4
Compare with Default Ruling
For a non-menstruating pilgrim, leaving without Tawaf al-Wada' incurs a dam. This contrast highlights the concession.
The principle: wajibat can be waived under genuine incapacity.

And if she menstruates after standing at 'Arafah and after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, she departs. (13)(19) If a woman menstruates after Wuquf at 'Arafah and after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, she may leave. Clarification: If she becomes menstruating after Wuquf at 'Arafah and after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, she will return from Mecca and nothing is due upon her for leaving Tawaf al-Wada'. Since she has performed the obligatory (Tawaf al-Ziyarah), and only Tawaf al-Wada' remains wajib, it is no longer obligatory for her, and no compensation is due.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This lesson presents the ruling for a woman who menstruates after performing the two key rites: standing at 'Arafah (Wuquf) and the obligatory tawaf (Tawaf al-Ziyarah). The matn simply says 'she departs' (انصرفت). The Urdu commentary explains that since the obligatory parts (fard) are complete, the remaining wajib (Tawaf al-Wada') is waived for her due to menstruation, and no dam or fidyah is required. This is a concession unique to menstruating women in Hajj.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed on the day of Eid or after, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah; it is a rukn of Hajj.
طواف الوداع (tawaf al-wada'): The farewell tawaf before leaving Mecca, wajib in the Hanafi school.

Ihram Before Hajj Months: Valid but Makruh
Ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on ihram before Hajj months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on ihram for Hajj before its months and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ihram for Hajj before its months is valid but makruh; the Shafi'i view that it becomes Umrah is rejected.

When is it permissible to enter ihram for Hajj? The months of Hajj are well-defined, but what if someone enters ihram earlier? The Hanafi school, based on an athar from Ibn Abbas, rules that such an ihram is valid but disliked. This lesson examines the proof, the Shafi'i opposition, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: ihram before the months is valid and Hajj is concluded, but the act is makruh tanzih (disliked).
Makruh here means against the Sunnah, not haram.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such ihram becomes Umrah, invalidating the Hajj.
The Shafi'i view is based on an athar from Ata.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the athar of Ibn Abbas and the athar of Ata commanding conversion to Umrah.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between indication of karahah and invalidity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that Ibn Abbas's statement only shows that the act is not from the Sunnah (karahah), not that it is invalid. The athar of Ata is not considered binding.
The Hanafi school relies on the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi who does this has a valid Hajj; a Shafi'i must treat it as Umrah and perform Hajj again.
This difference in rulings matters for actual practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدم الاحرام بالحج عليها جاز احرامه وانعقد حجه (۱) بالحج في غير اشهر الحج قال ليس ذلك من السنة (الف) (سن للبیھقی ، باب لا يصل بالج في غير اشهر الحج ج رابع ص ۱۵۶۱، نمبر ۸۷۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اشھر حج سے پہلے حج کا احرام باندھے تو وہ سنت کے خلاف ہے یعنی مکروہ ہے۔ تاہم حج کا احترام ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اشہر حج سے پہلے احرام باندھا تو حج نہیں ہوگا وہ عمرہ کے احترام میں تبدیل ہو جائے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یا اثر ہے عن عطاء قال من احرم بالج في غير اشهر الحج جعلها عمرة (ب) ( سنن سيحقی ، باب لا يصل بالج فی غیر اشهر الحج ج رابع ص ۱۵۶۱، نمبر ۸۷۲۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اشہر حج کے علاوہ میں حج کا احرام باندھے تو اس کو عمرہ بنادے (۲) اوپر کا عبد اللہ بن عباس کا اثر بھی امام شافعی کی دلیل ہے۔ [۱۲] حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عباس سے منقول ہے کہ وہ آدمی جو اشہر حج کے علاوہ میں احرام باندھے، فرمایا یہ سنت میں سے نہیں ہے ( ب ) حضرت عطا فر ماتے ہیں کہ جس نے اشہر حج کے علاوہ میں حج کا احرام باندھا تو اس کو عمرہ بنادے
He introduced ihram for Hajj upon it, so his ihram is valid and his Hajj is concluded. (1) He performed Hajj outside the months of Hajj, he said that is not from the Sunnah. (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...) From this athar it is known that if one binds ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj, it is against the Sunnah, i.e., makruh. However, his Hajj will be valid. Imam Shafi'i says that if he binds ihram before the months of Hajj, the Hajj will not be valid, it will turn into Umrah. Their evidence is the athar from Ata: 'Whoever binds ihram for Hajj outside the months of Hajj, he should make it Umrah.' (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...) From this athar it is known that if he binds ihram for Hajj outside the months of Hajj, he should make it Umrah. (2) The above athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas is also evidence for Imam Shafi'i. [12] Footnote: (a) It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that a man who binds ihram outside the months of Hajj, he said this is not from the Sunnah. (b) Ata said: Whoever binds ihram for Hajj outside the months of Hajj, he should make it Umrah.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on performing ihram for Hajj before the designated months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah). The Hanafi position, based on the athar of Ibn Abbas, states that such an ihram is valid and the Hajj is concluded, but the action is makruh (disliked) because it is against the Sunnah. The commentator explains that although it is makruh, the Hajj is still valid and does not turn into Umrah. In contrast, Imam Shafi'i holds that ihram for Hajj outside its months is invalid and automatically becomes an Ihram for Umrah. His evidence is the athar from Ata, which commands converting it to Umrah. The commentator notes that the athar of Ibn Abbas is also used by Shafi'i as evidence. The footnote clarifies the sources of these athar. The Hanafi position here is that the ruling of validity with karahah is the mufta bihi position, while the Shafi'i view is rejected. The authority_weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah.
مكروه (makruh): An act that is disliked and contrary to the Sunnah, but not sinful enough to invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ihram is invalid and becomes Umrah.
B) The ihram is valid and the Hajj is concluded, but it is makruh.
C) The ihram is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The ihram is valid and recommended.

Key Takeaway
Ihram for Hajj before the months is valid but makruh; the Shafi'i view that it becomes Umrah is not accepted in the Hanafi school.

Menstruating Woman at Ihram: The Exception of Tawaf
Ruling with proof for menstruating woman at ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a menstruating woman at the time of ihram and identify the proof from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
She performs all Hajj rites except tawaf until pure; the hadith explicitly exempts tawaf.

This lesson addresses the first scenario: a woman menstruates at the moment of ihram. The Hanafi School provides clear guidance based on the hadith of Aisha (ra). You will learn the exact procedure and the legal reasoning behind the exception of tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The woman is about to enter ihram but menstruates. What must she do first?
She must perform ghusl before ihram.
2
State the rule
She performs all Hajj actions except tawaf until she becomes pure. Why is tawaf excluded?
Because tawaf requires entering the mosque, which is prohibited for a menstruating woman.
3
Locate the proof
The proof is the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet told her to do all Hajj except tawaf. Identify the key phrase.
The phrase 'غير ان لا تطوفى بالبيت حتى تغتسلى' is the explicit exception.
4
Analyse the dalala
The command 'اقضي ما يقضى الحج' is general, but the exception is specific. Understand how the Hanafi school derives the ruling from this text.
The exception is qat'i al-dalala in excluding tawaf.

حرج نہیں ہے، واپس چلو۔
And if the woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs ghusl, binds ihram, and does as the pilgrim does except that she does not perform tawaf around the House until she becomes pure. 13 (19) And if she menstruates after standing at Arafah and after tawaf al-ziyarah, she departs from Makkah and nothing is upon her for leaving tawaf al-sudr. (18) If a woman becomes menstruating at the time of ihram, she should perform ghusl, bind ihram, and perform the same actions as the pilgrim does, except that she should not perform tawaf of the Kaaba until she becomes pure. Since all actions of Hajj except tawaf take place in the open, the menstruating woman can do them; however, tawaf takes place in the Masjid al-Haram and a menstruating woman cannot enter the mosque, so she will not perform tawaf. She will perform all remaining actions of Hajj. (2) There is also proof in the hadith from Aisha who said: We set out with the Prophet... He said: 'Are you menstruating?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'This is something Allah has written upon the daughters of Adam. So perform what the pilgrim performs, except do not perform tawaf of the House until you perform ghusl.' She said: And the Messenger of Allah sacrificed a cow for his wives. (c) (Muslim... Bukhari...) From this hadith it is known that a menstruating or postpartum woman will bind ihram for Hajj but will not perform tawaf. 13 (19) If she menstruates after standing at Arafah and after tawaf al-ziyarah, she will return from Makkah and nothing is required of her for leaving tawaf al-wada. Since she performed tawaf al-ziyarah, the obligatory act is done and only the wajib tawaf al-wada remains, so she leaves it and returns home. Since tawaf al-wada is wajib, there is no dam for leaving it. From Aisha: We set out with the Prophet... and Safiyyah bint Huyayy menstruated. The Prophet said: 'You have detained us! Did you perform tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then there is no harm, depart.' (a) (Bukhari... Muslim...) From this hadith it is known that if menstruation occurs after tawaf al-ziyarah and there is no opportunity for tawaf al-wada, then tawaf al-wada is dropped for the menstruating woman. And if she menstruated before tawaf al-ziyarah, since she already performed wuquf at Arafah, the Hajj is valid. However, tawaf al-ziyarah which is fard remains. So she should stay for tawaf al-ziyarah, or when possible perform it and give dam. If no opportunity arises, she should appoint someone to perform tawaf al-ziyarah on her behalf. Footnote: (c) Aisha said: We set out with the Prophet... He said: 'Are you menstruating?' I said: 'Yes.' He said: 'This is something Allah has written upon the daughters of Adam. So perform what the pilgrim performs, except do not perform tawaf of the House until you perform ghusl.' She said: And the Messenger of Allah sacrificed a cow for his wives. Footnote: (a) Safiyyah menstruated, so the Prophet said: 'May you be bereaved! You have detained us. Did you perform tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then there is no harm, depart.'
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings for a menstruating woman during Hajj, each with proofs. The first ruling: at the time of ihram, she performs ghusl, binds ihram, and does all Hajj actions except tawaf until she becomes pure, because tawaf requires entering the mosque which is prohibited for a menstruating woman. The proof is the famous hadith of Aisha in which the Prophet explicitly told her to do all Hajj actions except tawaf. The second ruling: if she menstruates after wuquf and after having performed tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf), she may depart from Makkah and does not owe anything for leaving tawaf al-wada, which is wajib. This is based on the hadith of Safiyyah, where the Prophet allowed her to depart after confirming she had done tawaf al-ziyarah. However, if she menstruates before performing tawaf al-ziyarah, she must stay until she is pure and performs it, or if not possible, appoint a proxy. The commentary explains the logic: since tawaf al-ziyarah is fard, it cannot be abandoned without compensation, whereas tawaf al-wada is only wajib and is waived for the menstruating woman. The authority_weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as the rulings are based on sound hadith and are standard Hanafi positions.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah) or thereafter, which is a rukn of Hajj.
طواف الصدر (الوداع) (tawaf al-sudr (al-wada')): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Makkah, which is wajib in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) She can perform tawaf and then give a dam.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman performs all Hajj rites except tawaf until she becomes pure, based on the explicit exemption in the hadith of Aisha.

Menstruating Woman After Wuquf and Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Dropping Tawaf al-Wada
Ruling with proof for menstruating woman after tawaf al-ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why tawaf al-wada is dropped for a menstruating woman after tawaf al-ziyarah and derive the ruling from the hadith of Safiyyah.

Core Idea
If she performs tawaf al-ziyarah and then menstruates, she may depart without tawaf al-wada because it is wajib, not fard.

This lesson covers the second scenario: a woman completes wuquf and tawaf al-ziyarah, then menstruates. The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith of Safiyyah, exempts her from tawaf al-wada. You will learn the distinction between fard and wajib and how it affects the Hajj of a menstruating woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The woman has performed wuquf at Arafah and tawaf al-ziyarah (the fard tawaf). Then she menstruates before performing tawaf al-wada.
Tawaf al-ziyarah is already done, so the main fard is complete.
2
State the ruling
She may depart from Makkah without performing tawaf al-wada, and she owes no penalty (dam). Why?
Because tawaf al-wada is wajib, not fard, and is waived for a valid excuse (menstruation).
3
Locate the proof
The proof is the hadith of Safiyyah bint Huyayy. When she menstruated after tawaf al-ziyarah, the Prophet allowed her to depart.
The Prophet said: 'Did you perform tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice?' She said 'Yes.' He said: 'Then there is no harm, depart.'
4
Analyse the exception
Understand the fiqh principle that a wajib can be dropped for a valid excuse, whereas a fard cannot. Tawaf al-wada is wajib, so it is dropped here.
If tawaf al-ziyarah were not done, the Hajj would be incomplete; she would have to stay or deputize.

And if the woman menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs ghusl, binds ihram, and does as the pilgrim does except that she does not perform tawaf around the House until she becomes pure. 13 (19) And if she menstruates after standing at Arafah and after tawaf al-ziyarah, she departs from Makkah and nothing is upon her for leaving tawaf al-sudr. (18) If a woman becomes menstruating at the time of ihram, she should perform ghusl, bind ihram, and perform the same actions as the pilgrim does, except that she should not perform tawaf of the Kaaba until she becomes pure. Since all actions of Hajj except tawaf take place in the open, the menstruating woman can do them; however, tawaf takes place in the Masjid al-Haram and a menstruating woman cannot enter the mosque, so she will not perform tawaf. She will perform all remaining actions of Hajj. (2) There is also proof in the hadith from Aisha who said: We set out with the Prophet... He said: 'Are you menstruating?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'This is something Allah has written upon the daughters of Adam. So perform what the pilgrim performs, except do not perform tawaf of the House until you perform ghusl.' She said: And the Messenger of Allah sacrificed a cow for his wives. (c) (Muslim... Bukhari...) From this hadith it is known that a menstruating or postpartum woman will bind ihram for Hajj but will not perform tawaf. 13 (19) If she menstruates after standing at Arafah and after tawaf al-ziyarah, she will return from Makkah and nothing is required of her for leaving tawaf al-wada. Since she performed tawaf al-ziyarah, the obligatory act is done and only the wajib tawaf al-wada remains, so she leaves it and returns home. Since tawaf al-wada is wajib, there is no dam for leaving it. From Aisha: We set out with the Prophet... and Safiyyah bint Huyayy menstruated. The Prophet said: 'You have detained us! Did you perform tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then there is no harm, depart.' (a) (Bukhari... Muslim...) From this hadith it is known that if menstruation occurs after tawaf al-ziyarah and there is no opportunity for tawaf al-wada, then tawaf al-wada is dropped for the menstruating woman. And if she menstruated before tawaf al-ziyarah, since she already performed wuquf at Arafah, the Hajj is valid. However, tawaf al-ziyarah which is fard remains. So she should stay for tawaf al-ziyarah, or when possible perform it and give dam. If no opportunity arises, she should appoint someone to perform tawaf al-ziyarah on her behalf. Footnote: (c) Aisha said: We set out with the Prophet... He said: 'Are you menstruating?' I said: 'Yes.' He said: 'This is something Allah has written upon the daughters of Adam. So perform what the pilgrim performs, except do not perform tawaf of the House until you perform ghusl.' She said: And the Messenger of Allah sacrificed a cow for his wives. Footnote: (a) Safiyyah menstruated, so the Prophet said: 'May you be bereaved! You have detained us. Did you perform tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then there is no harm, depart.'
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings for a menstruating woman during Hajj, each with proofs. The first ruling: at the time of ihram, she performs ghusl, binds ihram, and does all Hajj actions except tawaf until she becomes pure, because tawaf requires entering the mosque which is prohibited for a menstruating woman. The proof is the famous hadith of Aisha in which the Prophet explicitly told her to do all Hajj actions except tawaf. The second ruling: if she menstruates after wuquf and after having performed tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf), she may depart from Makkah and does not owe anything for leaving tawaf al-wada, which is wajib. This is based on the hadith of Safiyyah, where the Prophet allowed her to depart after confirming she had done tawaf al-ziyarah. However, if she menstruates before performing tawaf al-ziyarah, she must stay until she is pure and performs it, or if not possible, appoint a proxy. The commentary explains the logic: since tawaf al-ziyarah is fard, it cannot be abandoned without compensation, whereas tawaf al-wada is only wajib and is waived for the menstruating woman. The authority_weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as the rulings are based on sound hadith and are standard Hanafi positions.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah) or thereafter, which is a rukn of Hajj.
طواف الصدر (الوداع) (tawaf al-sudr (al-wada')): The farewell tawaf performed when leaving Makkah, which is wajib in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a woman menstruates after performing tawaf al-ziyarah?
A) She must stay until pure and then perform tawaf al-wada.
B) She must give a dam and leave.
C) She may leave without performing tawaf al-wada and owes nothing.
D) Her Hajj is invalid and she must repeat it.

Key Takeaway
If a woman menstruates after tawaf al-ziyarah, tawaf al-wada is dropped and she may depart without penalty, because it is wajib, not fard.

Tawaf al-Wada' Dropped for Menstruating Woman
Ruling and proof for dropping Tawaf al-Wada' for a menstruating woman after Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Wada' for a menstruating woman and apply the proof from the hadith of Safiyyah.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib but waived for menstruating women who have performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

This passage addresses a crucial practical scenario in Hajj: a woman who menstruates after performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah and cannot perform Tawaf al-Wada'. The Hanafi school rules that Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib, but it is dropped for the menstruating woman, and no compensation (dam) is required. The proof is the prophetic example with Safiyyah. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what Tawaf al-Wada' is and its hukm level in the Hanafi school (wajib or fard?).
It is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
2
Note the exception
Under what condition is Tawaf al-Wada' dropped? For whom and after which previous act?
It is dropped for a menstruating woman who has performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
3
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary proof cited: the hadith of Safiyyah from Bukhari and Muslim.
The Prophet permitted Safiyyah to leave after Tawaf al-Ziyarah despite menstruation.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: The Prophet's permission implies Tawaf al-Wada' is not required of her.
The absence of a command to wait indicates the obligation is lifted.
5
Contrast with Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Notice why Tawaf al-Ziyarah is not waived even in menstruation: it is fard, not wajib.
The hadith shows the Prophet would have waited if she had not performed it.

Source Text

From Makkah, and nothing is required from her for leaving Tawaf al-Wada'. The Book of Hajj. She leaves [Makkah] and returns home. Since Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib, leaving it does not require a dam. From Aisha, she said: We went out with the Prophet, and we only saw Hajj... and Safiyyah bint Huyayy menstruated, so the Prophet said: 'May your head be shaved, may your waist be cut, you have detained us! Did you perform Tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then no harm, leave.' (Bukhari, Bab idha hadat al-mar'atu ba'da ma afadat, p. 237, no. 1762; Muslim, Bab wujub tawaf al-wada' wa suqutuhu 'an al-ha'id, p. 427, no. 1762). From this hadith, it is understood that if menstruation occurs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and there is no opportunity for Tawaf al-Wada', Tawaf al-Wada' is waived for the menstruating woman. But if she menstruates without performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, since she has performed Wuquf at Arafah, her Hajj is valid. However, Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which is fard, remains. Therefore, she must wait for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, or perform it when possible and give a dam. If she cannot find an opportunity, she should have someone else perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah on her behalf. In the above hadith, regarding Sayyidah Safiyyah, it became clear that when she menstruated, the Prophet expressed regret: if she had not performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah, we would have to wait. But when he learned that she had performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he said: 'Now there is no harm.' From this, it is understood that one must wait for Tawaf al-Ziyarah because it is fard. And if Tawaf al-Ziyarah remains outstanding, its substitution is required. The proof is this athar: From Hasan regarding a man who enters ihram and dies before completing his rites, he said: 'What remains of his rites should be performed on his behalf.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 216, Fi al-rajul yamutu wa qad baqiya 'alayhi min nusukihi shay', vol. 3, p. 261, no. 14117). Footnote (a): Sayyidah Safiyyah menstruated, so the Prophet said: 'May your mother lose you, you have detained me! Have you performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah?' Safiyyah said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then there is no harm, go back.'
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Wada' (farewell tawaf) for a menstruating woman. The opening line states that a woman who leaves Makkah without performing Tawaf al-Wada' has no liability (no dam) because it is wajib, not fard—and in the Hanafi school, omission of a wajib in Hajj requires dam only if it is a deliberate act of omission of a pillar? Actually here the text says 'nothing upon her for leaving Tawaf al-Sadr' (another name for Tawaf al-Wada'). The author explains that since Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib, leaving it does not necessitate dam? This seems contradictory to standard Hanafi ruling: usually leaving a wajib requires dam. However, the context is a woman who has already performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah and then menstruates; the text clarifies that if she cannot perform Tawaf al-Wada' due to menstruation, it is waived (saqit) and no dam is required. The proof is the hadith of Safiyyah. The passage then contrasts the case if she has not performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah (which is fard): she must wait or have it done by proxy. This is a ruling with proof: the hadith from Aisha and the athar from Hasan al-Basri establish that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is fard and must be fulfilled even after death, so by analogy, if she cannot do it herself, someone else should do it for her. The footnote further clarifies that the Prophet's concern was about Tawaf al-Ziyarah, not Tawaf al-Wada'.

Key Terms
طواف الوداع (Tawaf al-Wada'): The farewell circumambulation performed upon leaving Makkah; wajib in the Hanafi school.
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation performed after Wuquf on the Day of Sacrifice; fard in Hajj.
حائض (ha'id): A woman experiencing menstruation; certain ritual acts are prohibited or waived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a menstruating woman who performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah but leaves Makkah without Tawaf al-Wada'?
A) She must give a dam
B) It is waived and no dam is required
C) She must perform it after menstruation
D) She must send a proxy

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib but specifically waived for menstruating women who have performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah, with no compensation needed.

Perfume on a Full Limb Incurs Dam for Muhrim
Ruling and proof that a Muhrim applying perfume to a full limb or more requires dam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Muhrim applying perfume and identify the threshold (full limb) that triggers the obligation of dam, with evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Perfuming a full limb or more in ihram requires one dam; the same type of violation merges (tadakhul).

This passage from the chapter on Hajj violations establishes a key ruling: if a Muhrim applies perfume to at least one complete limb, he must offer a dam. The text distinguishes between a full limb (requiring dam) and less than a limb (requiring sadaqah). It also introduces tadakhul – if multiple limbs are perfumed, they count as one violation. The ruling is proven by hadiths that explicitly prohibit perfume in ihram and by athar from Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is applying perfume while in ihram. The ruling specifies kaffarah: for a full limb or more, dam; for less than a limb, sadaqah.
The prohibition of perfume itself is haram; the dam is wajib compensation.
2
Locate the dalil
The prohibition is from the hadith of Yala ibn Umayyah (Bukhari/Muslim) and Ibn Umar (Bukhari). The kaffarah is derived from athar of Jabir and Ata.
The prophetic command to wash off perfume indicates prohibition; the specific dam amount is from the practice of the Companions.
3
Understand the threshold
The text limits dam to a complete limb or more. This is based on qiyas with shaving hair (dam for quarter head) and the principle that significant violations require greater compensation.
A full limb means an entire hand, foot, arm, leg, or head.
4
Apply tadakhul
If multiple limbs are perfumed, they merge into one violation because it is the same type (perfume). Only one dam is required.
Tadakhul applies when the violations are of the same category and occur in a single act.
5
Note cross-madhhab view
The Shafi'i school also requires fidyah but does not have a limb threshold; any perfume requires compensation. The Hanafi view is based on the text and qiyas.
Practical consequence: Hanafi mufta bihi is dam for full limb or more, sadaqah for less.
