The nails of one hand are five nails, but if he cuts five nails from different hands and feet, then according to the two shaykhs, sadaqah will be obligatory. And according to Imam Muhammad, dam will be obligatory. The two shaykhs say: cutting nails from different hands and feet is not beautification; rather it is ugliness (badnumai), and in Sharia, at the time of ihram, beautification is not permissible, and this became ugliness, so it cannot be considered a quarter of all nails, therefore sadaqah is obligatory. (b) Hadrat Hasan and Ata said: If a nail breaks, he cuts it from where it broke, then nothing is on him. But if he cuts it before it breaks, then dam is necessary.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the penalty for cutting five nails that are scattered across different hands and feet. The matn states the positions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say sadaqah, while Imam Muhammad says dam. The commentary explains the reasoning: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that cutting scattered nails does not constitute beautification (zinat) but rather ugliness (badnumai), and since beautification is prohibited in ihram, the act here is not considered beautification, so the penalty is sadaqah. They do not treat scattered nails as a quarter of the nails. Imam Muhammad, by analogy to shaving a quarter of the head, treats five nails (which are a quarter of all nails) as requiring dam, regardless of whether they are from one limb or scattered. The passage also includes an athar from Malik and from Hasan/Ata to support the general prohibition of nail cutting in ihram.

Key Terms
پراگندگی (paragandagi): Dishevelment; the state of being unkempt, which is recommended for a muhrim.
بدنمائی (badnumai): Ugliness; the opposite of beautification; the two shaykhs argue that cutting scattered nails causes ugliness, not beautification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the penalty for a muhrim who cuts five nails scattered across different hands and feet according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
Dam
Sadaqah
Fasting three days
No penalty

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, cutting scattered nails in ihram triggers sadaqah (not dam) according to the two shaykhs, because the act is considered ugliness rather than beautification.

Ruling on Excused Violations of Ihram: Choice of Expiation
Provides a choice of expiation for muhrim who violates due to excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of expiation for a muhrim who violates ihram due to an excuse, cite the Quranic and Hadith evidence, and apply the ruling to a new scenario.

Core Idea
A muhrim with a valid excuse may choose: sacrifice a sheep, feed six poor with three sa', or fast three days.

Hajj requires strict adherence to ihram prohibitions, but Islamic law accommodates genuine hardship. When a pilgrim faces a valid excuse—like illness, head ailment, or extreme heat—and applies perfume, shaves, or wears stitched clothes, the law does not impose a fixed expiation. Instead, it grants a merciful choice among three equally valid compensations. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its scriptural foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the violation and the excuse
Locate the three forbidden acts (perfume, shaving, stitched clothes) and the condition that triggers the choice: a legitimate excuse (udhr). Without an excuse, the ruling is different.
The excuse must be genuine, not trivial. The Hanafi school considers lice, illness, or extreme heat as valid.
2
State the ruling: three options
The muhrim may choose (takhayyur) among three forms of expiation: sacrificing a sheep (dam), feeding six poor people with three sa' of food (sadaqah), or fasting three days.
The food measure is three sa'—approximately 7.2 kg of wheat or equivalent.
3
Cite the Quranic evidence
Refer to Surah al-Baqarah 2:196: 'Then whoever among you is ill or has an ailment in his head, then a compensation of fasting or charity or sacrifice.' This verse is the primary textual proof.
The verse uses the conjunction 'aw' (or) indicating choice, not combination.
4
Cite the Hadith evidence
The hadith of Ka'b bin Ujrah confirms the verse's application. The Prophet ﷺ told him to shave due to lice and then fast three days, give charity to six people, or offer a sacrifice.
The hadith specifies six poor people for charity, which the Hanafis interpret as the default.
5
Note the epistemological weight
The Quranic text is qat'i in transmission (thubut) but zanni in meaning (dalala) regarding choice. The Hadith is ahad but widely accepted. The Hanafi school accepts this as zahir al-riwayah.
No explicit tarjih is needed; all major Hanafi authorities agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(11) And if he applies perfume, or shaves, or wears sewn clothes due to an excuse, then he has a choice: if he wishes, he sacrifices a sheep; if he wishes, he gives charity to six poor people with three sa' of food; and if he wishes, he fasts three days. [752] (11) If due to an excuse he applied perfume, or had his head shaved, or wore sewn clothes, then he has a choice: either he sacrifices a goat, or he gives charity to six poor people with three sa' of food, or he fasts three days. The verse mentions that if he shaves his head due to an excuse, he has a choice among these three: either sacrifice a goat, or give three sa' of wheat to six poor people as charity, or fast three days. (2) The verse is: 'Then whoever among you is ill or has an ailment in his head, then a compensation of fasting or charity or sacrifice' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:196). This verse mentions that if there is discomfort in the head, he may shave his head and do one of three things. (3) In the hadith: Ka'b bin Ujrah narrated that the Messenger of Allah stood before him at Hudaybiyyah and his head was swarming with lice. He said: 'Are your lice troubling you?' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Shave your head' or 'Have it shaved.' He said: Then this verse was revealed: 'Then whoever among you is ill...' Then the Prophet said: 'Fast three days, or give charity to six people with a farq, or sacrifice what is available.' (Bukhari, chapter on the saying of Allah 'or charity' and it is six poor people, p. 244, no. 1815; Muslim, chapter on permissibility of shaving head for a muhrim if there is harm, p. 382, no. 120). From this hadith it is learned that if there is an excuse and he does an act contrary to ihram, he has a choice among sadaqah, fasting, or sacrifice.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a muhrim who, due to a valid excuse (such as illness or head ailment), performs one of three prohibited acts: applying perfume, shaving the head, or wearing sewn clothes. The ruling provides a choice of expiation: sacrificing a sheep, feeding six poor people with three sa' of food, or fasting three days. The commentary supports this with the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196) and the hadith of Ka'b bin Ujrah, which specifically dealt with shaving due to lice. The verse gives a general principle, and the hadith applies it to the case of shaving. The commentary notes that this ruling is based on the Quran and Sunnah, and the choice is given to the person.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse, such as illness or harm, that permits a muhrim to violate ihram restrictions with expiation.
فرق (farq): A measure of food; in the hadith, it is used interchangeably with three sa'.

D) Only fasting

Key Takeaway
A muhrim who violates ihram due to a valid excuse has the choice of sacrificing a sheep, feeding six poor with three sa', or fasting three days.

Kissing or Touching with Desire in Ihram
Ruling with proof from Companions' sayings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muhrim who kisses or touches with desire, identify the evidence from the Companions, and apply the rule regardless of emission.

Core Idea
Kissing or touching with desire in ihram requires dam—even without ejaculation.

This lesson clarifies an important ruling on actions that violate ihram without reaching the level of full intercourse. The Hanafi school holds that any intentional sexual contact with desire incurs a dam, regardless of whether emission occurs. The evidence comes from the practice of the Companions, as recorded in the athar of Ali and Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is kissing or touching with desire. The hukm is that dam (blood sacrifice) is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Two athar: one from Ali and one from Ibn Abbas, both stating that a muhrim who kisses must 'spill blood' (give a dam).
These are from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Kitab al-Athar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The imperative phrase 'falyuhriq daman' (let him spill blood) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The athar are zanni in thubut and dalala, hence the hukm is wajib, not fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Some other schools may differentiate based on emission, but the Hanafi position is consistent: dam is required whether ejaculation occurs or not.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf_fih.
5
Evaluate the authority
How strong is the evidence? The athar are from Sahaba, but they are ahad (single transmission). The Hanafi school relies on them with the principle that qawl sahabi is a source of law (madhhab al-sahabi hujja).
This ruling is from zahir al-riwayah.

From this athar it is learned that if a woman is kissed, dam becomes obligatory. (2) In Imam Muhammad's Kitab al-Athar, p. 53, there is also an athar from Ibn Abbas that dam is necessary.

This passage rules that a muhrim who kisses or touches his spouse with sexual desire must offer a dam (blood sacrifice), regardless of whether ejaculation occurs. The proof comes from athar (sayings of the Companions): one from Ali ibn Abi Talib and another from Ibn Abbas, both indicating that such actions require a dam. The commentary explains that these athar serve as evidence for the ruling.

Key Terms
شهوة (shahwah): Sexual desire; the ruling applies when the act is done with desire, not merely accidentally.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice; one of the penalties (jaza) for violating the prohibitions of ihram.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram (ritual consecration) for Hajj or Umrah.

Ruling on Intercourse Before Wuquf in Hajj
Ruling statement with condition and penalty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse before Wuquf of Arafah and identify the required expiation.

Core Idea
Intercourse before Wuquf invalidates Hajj (fasid) and requires a sheep as dam.

In the Hajj, certain acts violate the state of ihram and carry serious consequences. One of the most severe violations is sexual intercourse before the essential rite of Wuquf (standing) at Arafah. This lesson presents the clear Hanafi ruling on this matter, distinguishing it from other ihram violations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The ruling addresses sexual intercourse (جماع) in either the front or back passage. The key condition is that it occurs before the Wuquf at Arafah, which is the pillar (rukn) of Hajj.
After Wuquf, the ruling differs.
2
State the Hanafi hukm level
The Hajj becomes 'fasid' (invalid). In Hanafi terminology, this means the act is ruined but must be completed and then repeated in a subsequent year (qada).
Fasid is distinct from batil; here the Hajj is still to be completed.
3
Identify the required expiation
The pilgrim must sacrifice a sheep (bakra) as dam (penalty). This is wajib.
The sheep is the minimum; some schools require a camel.
4
Note the practical consequence
The pilgrim must complete the current Hajj (though invalid) and then perform a new Hajj the following year as qada. The sheep is offered in addition.
Failure to do so does not remove the obligation.

Intercourse Before Arafah Invalidates Hajj
Ruling with proof about intercourse before Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intercourse before Arafah, identify the required actions, and distinguish the penalty from intercourse after Arafah.

Core Idea
Intercourse before Arafah invalidates Hajj but rites continue; a goat penalty and qada' are required.

This lesson addresses a critical violation during Hajj: intercourse before the essential standing at Arafah. The Hanafi school holds that the Hajj becomes invalid (fasid), yet the pilgrim must still complete the rites, offer a goat sacrifice, and perform makeup Hajj the next year. We will examine the ruling, its proofs from hadith and athar, and the distinction from intercourse after Arafah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (intercourse before wuqoof Arafah) and the legal consequence (Hajj becomes fasid). Note the required actions: continue rites, sacrifice a goat, and perform qada'.
The ruling applies to both spouses if both are in ihram.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites several proofs: a hadith from Yazid ibn Nu'aym, an athar from Ibn Abbas, a mursal hadith from Dar Qutni, and a Quranic verse (2:197). Identify each source and its chain.
The hadith from Judham tribe is the primary evidence; it explicitly commands qada' and sacrifice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof supports the ruling. For example, the command 'اقضيا نسككما' (make up your rites) indicates the original Hajj was invalid, requiring repetition.
The verse 'فلا رفث' (no sexual relations) is used as an indication (isharah) that intercourse invalidates Hajj.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that Hajj is not invalidated by intercourse before Arafah; instead, a camel must be sacrificed. Understand the basis of this disagreement.
The Hanafi position is considered the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the strength of the dalil and the school's tarjih, the mufta bihi is: Hajj becomes fasid, a goat suffices as penalty, and qada' is obligatory.
The penalty is lighter than after Arafah because the offense occurs before the Hajj is complete.

Source Text

میں ہے عن كعب بن عجرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأه وانه يسقط على وجهه ... او يهدى شاة او يصوم ثلثة ايام (بخاری شریف، باب النسک شاة ص ۲۴۴ کتاب العمرة نمبر ۱۸۱۷) اس حدیث میں بکری کو ہدی کہا گیا فرمایا ایک بکری ہدی دیں یا تین دن روزے رکھیں۔
Before standing at Arafah, his Hajj becomes invalid, and upon him is a goat, and he proceeds in the Hajj just as one who has not invalidated his Hajj proceeds, and upon him is its makeup. He continues in the Hajj, like the one who has not invalidated Hajj, and upon him is qada. Someone who has put on ihram for Hajj then has intercourse before or after (before Arafah) – his Hajj becomes invalid. However, he performs Umrah with that same ihram and becomes halal, and does all the actions that the pilgrims do, and makes up the Hajj the following year. And due to breaking the Hajj, a goat is required. The goat is required because qada of Hajj is required, so the offense is not severe but mild. If he has intercourse after standing at Arafah, the Hajj is complete, so no qada is required, thus the offense is not severe, so a camel is required. There is a hadith: Yazid bin Nu'aym informed me that a man from Judham had intercourse with his wife while they were both in ihram. The man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), so he said to them both: 'Complete your rites, offer a sacrificial animal, then return until you come to the place where you committed the act, then separate, and do not see each other, and upon you both is another Hajj. Then go until you are at the place where you committed the act, then put on ihram, complete your rites, and offer a sacrificial animal.' (Sunan Saeedi, chapter on what invalidates Hajj, vol. 5, p. 272, no. 9778) (2) From Ibn Abbas concerning a man who had intercourse with his wife while in ihram: He said: 'Complete your rites, return to your country, and when the next year comes, go out as pilgrims. When you put on ihram, separate and do not meet until you complete your rites, and offer a sacrificial animal.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what invalidates Hajj, vol. 5, p. 273, no. 9782) From this hadith and athar, it is understood that if one invalidates Hajj by intercourse before standing at Arafah, then he must make it up the next year and give a hadi. Also, the hadith of Dar Qutni: 'Whoever reaches Arafat and stands there and Muzdalifah, his Hajj is complete; and whoever misses Arafat, his Hajj is missed – let him become halal by performing Umrah, and upon him is Hajj the next year.' (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Hajj, no. 2497) This hadith indicates that if Hajj becomes invalid before Arafah, one should become halal by Umrah and do Hajj the next year. Since hadi is absolute, a goat suffices. (3) There is also an indication from the verse: 'So whoever has obligated Hajj therein, then no sexual relations, no wickedness, nor disputation during Hajj.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:197) The verse says not even to speak of intercourse, so he committed intercourse, thus his Hajj becomes invalid. By absolute hadi, a goat is meant. There is a hadith from Ka'b bin 'Ujrah that the Messenger of Allah saw him with lice falling on his face... 'or offer a goat, or fast three days.' (Bukhari, Kitab al-Umrah, chapter on sacrificing a goat, p. 244, no. 1817) In this hadith, a goat is called hadi, so it is understood that when hadi is said absolutely, a goat is meant. Footnote: (a) A man from Judham tribe had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram. He asked the Prophet, and he said to both: 'Make up your Hajj and give a sacrifice, then return home, and when you come to the place where you did the act, separate and do not see each other, and upon you both is another Hajj. So come until you are at the place where you did the act, then put on ihram and complete your Hajj and give a sacrifice.' (b) The Prophet saw Ka'b bin 'Ujrah with lice falling on his face, and said: 'Offer a goat as sacrifice or fast three days.'
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning intercourse before standing at Arafah (wuqoof) during Hajj. The author states the ruling: if a person engaged in intercourse before the wuqoof of Arafah, his Hajj becomes null and void (fasid). He must still continue the rites of Hajj, as he would have if it were valid, but he is required to sacrifice a goat (shah) as a penalty and must make up the Hajj the following year (qada). The commentary explains that if someone in ihram for Hajj has intercourse before or after (i.e., before Arafah), the Hajj becomes invalid. However, he can use that same ihram to perform Umrah and become halal, while continuing the actions of a pilgrim. The reason for the goat is that the penalty is lighter because qada is required; had the Hajj been complete (intercourse after Arafah), a camel would be required. The author then provides several proofs: a hadith from Yazid ibn Nu'aym from Sunan al-Bayhaqi about a man from Judham, an athar from Ibn Abbas, a mursal hadith from Dar Qutni, and a verse from the Quran (2:197) indicating that even speech of intercourse is forbidden, so doing it invalidates Hajj. Finally, the hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah establishes that the absolute term 'hadi' in the rulings refers to a goat. The footnote translates and explains the hadith and athar. This is a well-established ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
حج فاسد (hajj fasid): A Hajj that is invalid due to a violation like intercourse before Arafah; it requires continuation, penalty, and qada.
شاة (shah): A female goat, the minimum sacrificial animal for certain Hajj penalties.
قضاء (qada'): The obligatory makeup of a recommended or obligatory act that was invalidated or missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required penalty for intercourse before wuqoof Arafah that invalidates Hajj?
A) A camel
B) A goat
C) A cow
D) No penalty, only qada

Key Takeaway
Intercourse before Arafah invalidates Hajj, but the pilgrim must continue the rites, sacrifice a goat, and perform qada' the following year.

Separation from Wife During Qada Hajj
Hanafi ruling on separation of wife during makeup Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on separation of spouses during qada Hajj and explain the madhhab difference with the Shafi'i/Maliki view.

Core Idea
Separation of spouses during makeup Hajj is not required in the Hanafi school; it is caution, not obligation.

This passage addresses a disagreement among the schools regarding whether a person performing a makeup Hajj (qada) must physically separate from his wife. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Companions and a nuanced reading of the hadith, holds that it is not obligatory but merely recommended. In contrast, the Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider it mandatory. Understanding this difference hinges on the interpretive principle of whether a command indicates obligation or recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? According to the Hanafi school, what is the hukm regarding separating from one's wife during the makeup Hajj?
The Arabic matn explicitly states: 'وليس عليه ان يفارق امرأته' — it is not required upon him to separate.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
What proof does the Hanafi school cite? Look at the athar from Mujahid and ‘Ata’ mentioned in the commentary.
The athar: 'Upon them is Hajj the next year, and they do not separate.'
3
Understand the interpretation of the hadith
How does the Hanafi school interpret the hadith that commands separation? They view it as a recommendation for caution, not an obligation.
The command is to avoid repeated intercourse, not a mandatory requirement for validity.
4
State the opposing view
What do the Shafi'i and Maliki schools hold? What is their proof?
They take the hadith literally as an obligation to separate from ihram until tawaf al-ziyarah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in the performance of Hajj between the two views?
Hanafis allow the wife to accompany; Shafi'is and Malikis require separation, affecting travel arrangements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ اَنْ يُفَارِقَ اِمْرَأَتَهُ اِذَا حَجَّ بِهَا فِى الْقَضَاءِ عِنْدَنَا [۷۲۷] (۱۴) اور اس پر لازم نہیں ہے کہ بیوی کو جدا کرے جبکہ بیوی کے ساتھ قضاء حج کر رہا ہو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ جس وقت فاسد شدہ حج کی قضا کر رہا ہو تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس حج میں بیوی کو جدا کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ ساتھ رکھے گا تب بھی حج ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اوپر کی حدیث میں احرام باندھنے سے لیکر طواف زیارت تک بیوی کو جدا رکھنے کا حکم ہے وہ احتیاط کے لئے ہے تا کہ دوبارہ بیوی کے ساتھ جماع نہ کر بیٹھے۔ یہ احتیاط کر لے تو بہتر ہے۔ لیکن اگر بیوی کو ساتھ رکھے تو حج پر کچھ اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن مجاهد وعطاء قالا وعليهما الحج من قابل ولا يفرقان (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة، ۵۸ فی الرجل یواقع اهله وهو محرم، ج ثالث، ص ۱۶۰ نمبر ۱۳۰۸۵) ناں امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ احرام باندھنے کے بعد سے طواف زیارت تک بیوی کو جدا رکھے۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث ہے جس میں حکم ہے کہ بیوی کو حج کی قضا کرتے وقت علیحدہ رکھے۔
And it is not required upon him to separate from his wife when he performs Hajj with her in the qada, in our view. (14) And it is not necessary for him to separate his wife when he is performing qada Hajj with his wife, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. When he is making up an invalidated Hajj, according to Abu Hanifa it is not necessary to separate the wife in that Hajj. He may keep her with him and the Hajj will still be valid. The instruction in the previous hadith to keep the wife separate from the time of ihram until tawaf al-ziyarah is for caution, so that he does not have intercourse again. Doing this caution is better. But if he keeps his wife with him, it has no effect on the Hajj. There is an athar: From Mujahid and ‘Ata’: ‘And upon them is Hajj the next year, and they do not separate.’ (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 58, vol. 3, p. 160, no. 13085) Nay, according to Imam al-Shafi‘i and Imam Malik, he should separate from his wife from the time of ihram until tawaf al-ziyarah. Their proof is the hadith above which commands separation of the wife during qada Hajj.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab dispute about whether a person performing a makeup Hajj (qada) must separate from his wife. The Arabic matn states the Hanafi position: 'it is not required upon him to separate from his wife when he performs Hajj with her in the qada, in our view.' The Urdu commentary explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, separation is not obligatory; he may keep his wife with him and the Hajj remains valid. The hadith that orders separation is interpreted as a recommendation (caution) to avoid repeated intercourse. An athar from Mujahid and ‘Ata’ confirms: 'upon them is Hajj the next year, and they do not separate.' The opposing schools (Shafi‘i and Maliki) hold that separation is obligatory, citing the same hadith. The Hanafi response is that the command is for caution, not obligation. This clarifies the thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, Hanafis allow the wife to accompany the husband during the makeup Hajj without separation.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): The makeup Hajj performed the following year after invalidation of the original Hajj.
مفارقت (mufaraqat): Separation from one's spouse by avoiding contact or proximity; here, physical separation during the pilgrimage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on separating from one's wife during the makeup Hajj?
A) It is wajib
B) It is haram
C) It is not required; permissible to keep her
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Separation from one's wife during makeup Hajj is not obligatory in the Hanafi school; it is a recommended precaution.

Intercourse After Arafah: Hajj Valid, Penalty Required
Ruling with proof that intercourse after Arafah does not invalidate Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse after Arafah and identify the proof and penalty.

Core Idea
Intercourse after Arafah does not invalidate Hajj; but a camel is wajib.

This lesson examines a critical distinction in Hajj jurisprudence: the difference between violations that nullify the Hajj and those that incur a penalty but leave the Hajj valid. The passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri clarifies that intercourse after standing at Arafah – the essential pillar – does not break the Hajj, but because the pilgrim is still in ihram, a severe penalty (badana) applies. We will unpack the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (intercourse after wuqoof Arafah) and the two-part ruling: Hajj is valid, and a camel is required.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs cited: the athar of Ibn Abbas (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) and the hadith of Dar Qutni/Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the athar proves the ruling: it orders a camel but does not command qada, implying the Hajj is valid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that some scholars hold intercourse after Arafah invalidates Hajj; the Hanafi school disagrees.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that Hajj is valid and a camel is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ لَمْ يَفْسُدْ حَجُّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ بَدَنَةٌ [۷۲۸] (۱۵) جس نے وقوف عرفہ کے بعد جماع کیا تو اس کا حج فاسد نہیں ہوگا اور اس پر اونٹ لازم ہے۔ وقوف عرفہ کے بعد اور حلق سے پہلے بیوی سے جماع کیا تو حج تو ہو گیا کیونکہ وقوف عرفہ تو کر لیا ہے لیکن حلق سے پہلے بیوی حلال نہیں تھی اور نہ سلا ہوا کپڑا اور خوشبو حلال تھے اس لئے اس وقت جماع کیا تو جنایت سنگین ہے اس لئے اونٹ ذبح کرنا ہوگا۔ (1) عن ابن عباس ان رجلا اصاب من اهله قبل ان يطوف بالبيت يوم النحر فقال ينحران جزورا بينهما وليس عليهما الحج من قابل (سنن البیہقی، باب الرجل یصیب امرأته بعد الحلل الاول وقبل الثانی ج خاص ص ۲۷۹، نمبر ۱۹۸۰ موطا امام مالک باب هدى من اصاب احله قبل ان فیض ص ۴۰۶ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبة، ۵۹ کم علیه احد یا واحدا او اثنين ؟، ج ثالث، ص ۱۶۱، نمبر ۱۳۰۸۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقوف عرفہ کے بعد اور حلق سے پہلے جماع کرلے تو بدنہ یعنی اونٹ لازم ہوگا اور حج مکمل ہو جائے گا۔ اس کی قضا لازم نہیں ہے (۲) وقوف عرفہ کے بعد جماع کرنے سے حج فاسد نہیں ہوگا اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبر ۱۳ کی دار قطنی کی حدیث بھی ہے من ادرک عرفات فوقف بها والمزدلفة فقد تم حجه (دارقطني نمبر ۲۴۹۷ ترمذی شریف نمبر ۸۸۹)
And whoever has intercourse after standing at Arafah, his Hajj is not invalidated, and upon him is a camel. (15) Whoever has intercourse after standing at Arafah, his Hajj will not be invalid, and upon him is a camel obligatory. If he has intercourse with his wife after standing at Arafah and before shaving (halq), his Hajj is valid because he has already stood at Arafah. But before shaving, his wife is not yet halal, nor are sewn clothes and perfume halal. Therefore, if he has intercourse at that time, the offense is severe, so he must slaughter a camel. (1) From Ibn Abbas: A man had intercourse with his wife before tawaf on the day of sacrifice (10th Dhu al-Hijjah). He said: 'Let them both slaughter a camel between them, and upon them is no Hajj the next year.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on a man who has intercourse with his wife after the first halal and before the second, vol. special, p. 279, no. 1980; Muwatta Imam Malik, chapter on penalty of one who has intercourse before ifada, p. 406; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 59, vol. 3, p. 161, no. 13088) This athar indicates that if one has intercourse after Arafah and before shaving, then a badana (camel) is required and the Hajj is complete; no qada is necessary. (2) The proof that intercourse after Arafah does not invalidate Hajj is also the hadith of Dar Qutni mentioned in problem no. 13: 'Whoever reaches Arafat, stands there, and Muzdalifah, his Hajj is complete.' (Dar Qutni no. 2497, Tirmidhi no. 889)
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proof for intercourse after standing at Arafah. The matn states: 'and whoever has intercourse after standing at Arafah, his Hajj is not invalidated, and upon him is a camel.' The commentary explains that if one has intercourse after Arafah but before shaving (halq), the Hajj remains valid because the essential pillar (wuqoof) has been performed. However, the person is still in ihram until shaving and tawaf al-ziyarah, so the intercourse is a severe violation, requiring a camel (badana). The proof is an athar from Ibn Abbas: a man who had intercourse before tawaf on the day of sacrifice is instructed to slaughter a camel, and no qada is required. Additionally, the hadith from Dar Qutni (and Tirmidhi) is cited: 'Whoever reaches Arafat, stands there, and Muzdalifah, his Hajj is complete.' This indicates that the Hajj is not invalidated by intercourse after Arafah. The penalty escalates because the violation occurs at a time when the Pilgrim is otherwise very close to completion.

Key Terms
بدنة (badana): A camel, the required sacrificial animal for severe violations during Hajj.
وقوف عرفة (wuqoof 'Arafah): The essential pillar of Hajj: standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhu al-Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the penalty for intercourse after standing at Arafah but before shaving?
A) A goat
B) A camel
C) A cow
D) Nothing, no penalty

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after Arafah does not invalidate Hajj; a camel (badana) is wajib as a severe penalty.

Intercourse After Shaving in Hajj: The Reduced Penalty
Ruling on intercourse after shaving in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intercourse after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah, explain why the penalty is reduced to a goat, and identify the conditions that make the spouse halal.

Core Idea
After shaving, the spouse remains haram until tawaf al-ziyarah; intercourse at this stage requires a goat, not a camel.

In the previous lesson, we learned that intercourse before shaving invalidates Hajj and requires a camel. Here, we examine a milder violation: intercourse after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah. The passage explains that because some restrictions (perfume, sewn clothes) are already lifted, the penalty is reduced to a goat. Understanding this gradation is essential for determining the correct dam for various ihram violations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
The act is intercourse (jima) after shaving (halq) but before tawaf al-ziyarah.
Shaving is done after wuqoof Arafah, marking partial release from ihram.
2
Determine the ruling
State the hukm: the Hajj remains valid, but a penalty (dam) of a goat is wajib.
3
Understand the rationale
Why a goat instead of a camel? Because some ihram restrictions are already removed (perfume, sewn clothes), reducing the severity.
The spouse is not yet halal, but the overall violation is lighter.
4
Note the condition for spousal halal
The spouse only becomes halal after tawaf al-ziyarah, so intercourse before that still violates the remaining ihram.
This is why a penalty is still required.
5
Contrast with the footnote
The athar from Ibn Abbas about a camel may refer to a different scenario (before shaving or on the 10th before tawaf without specifying halq). The Hanafi position is consistent.

Source Text

وَمَنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْحَلْقِ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ [۷۲۹] (۱۶) جس نے حلق کرانے کے بعد جماع کیا اس پر بکری لازم ہے۔ حج میں حلق کرا چکا تھا لیکن ابھی طواف زیارت نہیں کیا تھا اور جماع کر لیا تو چونکہ ابھی عورت حلال نہیں ہوئی تھی اس لئے دم لازم ہوگا۔ لیکن خوشبو اور سلا ہوا کپڑا حلال ہو چکے تھے اس لئے جنابت میں تخفیف ہو گئی۔ اس لئے اونٹ کی بجائے بکری لازم ہوگی۔ حاشیہ: (الف) ابن عباس نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی دسویں ذی الحجہ کو بیت اللہ کے طواف سے پہلے جماع کرلے تو فرمایا کہ دونوں اونٹ ذبح کرے اور دونوں پر اگلے سال حج کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
And whoever has intercourse after shaving, upon him is a goat. (16) Whoever has intercourse after shaving, a goat is required upon him. He had already shaved in the Hajj, but had not yet performed tawaf al-ziyarah, and he had intercourse. Since his wife had not yet become halal, a dam (blood sacrifice) is required. But perfume and sewn clothes had become halal, so the offense is reduced. Therefore, instead of a camel, a goat is required. Footnote: (a) Ibn Abbas said: If a man has intercourse on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah before tawaf of the House, he said: 'Let them both slaughter a camel between them, and upon them both, Hajj the next year is not necessary.'
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for intercourse after shaving (halq) but before tawaf al-ziyarah. The Arabic matn states: 'And whoever has intercourse after shaving, upon him is a goat.' The Urdu commentary explains the rationale: the person has already shaved, so perfume and sewn clothes are halal, but the spouse is not yet halal until tawaf al-ziyarah. Hence the violation is milder than intercourse before shaving (which requires a camel), so a goat suffices. The footnote cites an athar from Ibn Abbas about a man who had intercourse on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah before tawaf: the penalty is a camel, but interestingly, no qada is required. This specific athar seems to contradict the gradation? However, the commentary reconciles by noting that the situation there is before tawaf but after shaving? Actually the footnote says 'before tawaf' and does not specify halq. It may be a different scenario. Nonetheless, the established Hanafi ruling is that after halq, the penalty is a goat.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, a required act after wuqoof Arafah marking partial exit from ihram.
طواف زیارت (tawaf al-ziyarah): The essential tawaf performed on the 10th or 11th of Dhu al-Hijjah, after which the spouse becomes halal.
شاة (shah): A goat, the required penalty for intercourse after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah.

Ruling on Not Separating from Wife during Qada Hajj
Hanafi position on wife separation in qada Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wife separation during qada Hajj and explain how the Hanafi school interprets the relevant hadith against the Shafi'i/Maliki view.

Core Idea
Separation from wife during qada Hajj is precautionary, not obligatory, in the Hanafi school.

When a Hajj is invalidated due to a violation, the qada (make-up) Hajj must be performed in the following year. A key question arises: must the husband separate from his wife during this make-up Hajj? The Hanafi school takes a lenient view, while the Shafi'i and Maliki schools require separation. This lesson examines the evidence and reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
State clearly that the Hanafi school does not require separation from the wife during qada Hajj. The ruling is that separation is not obligatory but a recommended precaution.
Refer to the matn: 'وليس عليه أن يفارق امرأته'
2
Identify the opponent's view
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools hold that the husband must separate from his wife from the moment of ihram until tawaf al-ziyarah during the qada Hajj.
This is based on a hadith commanding separation.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent relies on a hadith that orders the man to keep his wife separate during the period from ihram to tawaf al-ziyarah. Consider what this hadith explicitly says.
The exact text is not quoted here but is referenced.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that the hadith is for precaution (ihtiyat) to prevent further intercourse, not an obligation (wajib). Moreover, the athar from Mujahid and 'Ata states 'no separation' (la furqan), supporting the Hanafi view.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under the Hanafi school, a husband may keep his wife with him during qada Hajj without the Hajj being invalidated. Under the Shafi'i/Maliki view, separation is required; failure to separate would affect the validity.
This difference matters for couples performing make-up Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُفَارِقَ امْرَأَتَهُ إِذَا حَجَّ بِهَا فِي الْقَضَاءِ عِنْدَنَا اور اس پر لازم نہیں ہے کہ بیوی کو جدا کرے جبکہ بیوی کے ساتھ قضاء حج کر رہا ہو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ جس وقت فاسد شدہ حج کی قضا کر رہا ہو تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس حج میں بیوی کو جدا کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ ساتھ رکھے گا تب بھی حج ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اوپر کی حدیث میں احرام باندھنے سے لیکر طواف زیارت تک بیوی کو جدا رکھنے کا حکم ہے وہ احتیاط کے لئے ہے تا کہ دوبارہ بیوی کے ساتھ جماع نہ کر بیٹھے۔ یہ احتیاط کر لے تو بہتر ہے۔ لیکن اگر بیوی کو ساتھ رکھے تو حج پر کچھ اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ وَعَطَاءٍ قَالَا وَعَلَيْهِمَا الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ وَلَا فَرْقَانَ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة، ۵۸ فی الرجل یواقع اهله وهو محرم، ج ثالث، ص ۱۶۰ نمبر ۱۳۰۸۵) نان امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ احرام باندھنے کے بعد سے طواف زیارت تک بیوی کو جدا رکھے۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث ہے جس میں حکم ہے کہ بیوی کو حج کی قضا کرتے وقت علیحدہ رکھے۔
And it is not upon him to separate from his wife when he performs Hajj with her in the qada (make-up) according to us. [Urdu: and it is not necessary for him to separate from his wife when performing the qada of Hajj with her according to Imam Abu Hanifa. At the time of performing qada of a corrupted Hajj, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not necessary to separate from the wife in this Hajj. Even if he keeps her with him, the Hajj will be performed. In the above hadith, the command to keep the wife separate from the time of ihram until tawaf al-ziyarah is for precaution, so that he does not again commit intercourse with his wife. If he does this precaution, it is better. But if he keeps the wife with him, it will have no effect on the Hajj. In the athar: from Mujahid and 'Ata, who said: 'And upon both of them is Hajj from the next year, and no separation.' (Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 58/13085) Then: Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that after tying ihram until tawaf al-ziyarah, the wife should be kept separate. Their evidence is the above hadith which commands to keep the wife separate when performing qada of Hajj.]
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling states that according to the Hanafi school, a man performing the qada (make-up) of a previously corrupted Hajj is not required to separate from his wife. The author explains that the hadith commanding separation from the time of ihram until tawaf al-ziyarah is precautionary, not obligatory, to prevent further intercourse. Keeping her is permissible and does not affect the validity of the Hajj. The athar from Mujahid and 'Ata (used by the opponent) actually states that both must perform Hajj the following year with no separation (la furqan), which the Hanafis interpret as evidence against mandatory separation. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools, however, insist on separation during qada based on that hadith. The Hanafi position relies on the absence of an explicit command for separation in the qada context and the principle that precaution (ihtiyat) is not obligatory.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): The performance of a missed or invalidated act of worship after its prescribed time.
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by wearing specified garments and avoiding certain prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is obligatory.
B) No, it is not required, but it is a recommended precaution.
C) Yes, but only if they had intercourse during the original Hajj.
D) No, it is forbidden to separate.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a man performing qada Hajj is not required to separate from his wife; the precautionary hadith is not obligatory.

The Ruling on Intercourse after Halq during Hajj
Ruling with evidence on post-halq intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intercourse after halq and explain why the penalty is a sheep using the evidence from Ibn Abbas and the school's qiyas.

Core Idea
After halq, intercourse incurs a sheep penalty, not a camel, because partial tahallul reduces the severity.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hajj: intercourse after the first stage of tahallul (halq) but before tawaf al-ziyarah. Understanding this ruling illustrates how the Hanafi school weighs evidence from hadith and applies qiyas to derive a penalty proportional to the degree of ihram violation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: intercourse after halq (shaving) but before tawaf al-ziyarah. The ruling: Hajj is sahih, but a sheep (shah) is wajib as a penalty.
The penalty is not a camel because halq represents partial release from ihram.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a narration from Ibn Abbas about a man who had intercourse before tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice. In that narration, Ibn Abbas prescribed a camel.
The hadith is found in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and other collections.
3
Understand the author's interpretation
The author distinguishes between intercourse before halq (camel) and after halq (sheep). The absolute 'hady' in the second narration is interpreted as a sheep because the offense is less severe after some restrictions are lifted.
The author uses the second narration's absolute term to support a lighter penalty.
4
Apply qiyas (analogy)
After halq, perfume and stitched clothes become permissible. Since the violation is within a state of weakened ihram, the penalty is reduced proportionally.
This is a qiyas jaliy based on the severity of the violation.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that a sheep is required, not a camel. This is the relied-upon view in the school.
No intra-Hanafi difference is noted here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْحَلْقِ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ (۱۲) جس نے حلق کرانے کے بعد جماع کیا اس پر بکری لازم ہے۔ حج میں حلق کرا چکا تھا لیکن ابھی طواف زیارت نہیں کیا تھا اور جماع کر لیا تو چونکہ ابھی عورت حلال نہیں ہوئی تھی اس لئے دم لازم ہوگا۔ لیکن خوشبو اور سلا ہوا کپڑا حلال ہو چکے تھے اس لئے جنابت میں تخفیف ہو گئی۔ اس لئے اونٹ کی بجائے بکری لازم ہوگی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) ابن عباس نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی دسویں ذی الحجہ کو بیت اللہ کے طواف سے پہلے جماع کرلے تو فرمایا کہ دونوں اونٹ ذبح کرے اور دونوں پر اگلے سال حج کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عباس کے اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ملا ہے عن ابن عباس انه قال في الذي يصيب اهله قبل ان يفيض يعتمر ويهدى (الف) (سنن سبیھقی ، باب الرجل یصیب امراته بعد التحلل الاول وقبل الثانی ج خامس ص ۲۷۹، نمبر ۹۸۰۲) اس اثر میں ہدی مطلق ہے اس لئے یہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ حلق کے بعد اور طواف زیارت سے پہلے جماع کیا تو مطلق ہدی سے بکری مراد ہے۔
And whoever has intercourse after shaving (halq), upon him is a sheep. (12) [Urdu: Whoever has intercourse after doing halq, a goat is obligatory upon him. In Hajj, he had performed halq but had not yet done tawaf al-ziyarah, and he had intercourse. Since the woman had not yet become halal for him, a dam (penalty) is obligatory. But perfume and stitched clothes had become halal, so the offense is reduced. Therefore, instead of a camel, a goat is obligatory. Footnote (a): Ibn Abbas said: If a man has intercourse on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah before tawaf of the House, he said: Let both slaughter a camel, and there is no Hajj upon them the next year. An indication of this is found in the narration from Abdullah ibn Abbas: He said regarding one who has intercourse with his wife before ifada (tawaf), he should perform Umrah and offer a hady. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, 9802) In this narration, hady is absolute, so it can be said that after halq and before tawaf al-ziyarah, intercourse requires a sheep as per absolute hady.]
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for intercourse after shaving (halq) but before tawaf al-ziyarah. The Hajj is valid, but a penalty is required: a sheep (shah). The author explains the rationale: after halq, some ihram restrictions are lifted (perfume and stitched clothes become halal), so the offense is less severe than before halq, hence a lesser penalty (sheep instead of camel). The woman, however, is not yet halal for intercourse until tawaf al-ziyarah. The footnote cites Ibn Abbas's statement that a man who had intercourse before tawaf on the Day of Sacrifice must slaughter a camel, but that narration is interpreted as specific to pre-tawaf (which may be before halq or after?). The author concludes that the absolute hady in the second narration refers to a sheep, as it is the default for less severe violations.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving or trimming the hair after the sacrificial day, which begins the partial release from ihram (tahallul al-awwal).
شاة (shah): A sheep or goat, used as a penalty in Hajj for less severe violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A sheep
C) Nothing; it is permissible
D) Repeating the Hajj

Key Takeaway
After halq, the penalty for intercourse is a sheep because partial release from ihram reduces the severity of the violation.

Ruling on Intercourse in Umrah before Four Tawaf Circuits
Ruling with proof on pre-four circuits intercourse in Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse during Umrah before completing four circuits of tawaf, explain the evidence from hadith and qiyas, and compare the penalty with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Before the majority of tawaf, intercourse invalidates Umrah — a sheep suffices, not a camel.

This passage from the Hanafi matn and its commentary addresses a specific scenario: intercourse during Umrah before completing four circuits of tawaf. The ruling covers invalidation, the requirement to perform qada, and the obligation of a sheep as penalty. It also introduces a cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school regarding the type of animal. Understanding this ruling illustrates the Hanafi methodology of using qiyas and the concept of majority in ritual acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its threshold
What act is being considered? Intercourse during Umrah. What is the threshold before which it invalidates? Before four circuits of tawaf.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Umrah becomes fasid (invalid), qada is required, and a sheep is owed.
3
Understand the rationale: majority of tawaf
Four circuits is the majority of seven, so completing four means tawaf is essentially performed; less than four means it is as if not performed.
4
Examine the evidence: hadith and qiyas
The hadith of Ibn Abbas prescribes a camel for intercourse before taqsir. Hanafis use qiyas to argue that a sheep is appropriate for Umrah because it is lesser than Hajj.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Shafi'is require a camel for invalidating Umrah. Hanafi response distinguishes the hadith's context.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ جَامَعَ فِي الْعُمْرَةِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَطُوفَ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ أَفْسَدَهَا وَقَضَاهَا وَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ جس نے چار شوطا طواف کرنے سے پہلے عمرہ میں جماع کیا تو اس نے عمرہ فاسد کر دیا اس لئے وہ عمرہ میں گزرتا رہے گا اور اس کو قضا کرے گا اور اس پر ایک بکری لازم ہے۔ چار شوط طواف کرلے تو سات طواف میں سے اکثر ہو گیا تو گویا کہ فرض کی ادائیگی ہو گئی۔ لیکن اگر چارشوط سے کم طواف کیا تو گویا کہ طواف کیا ہی نہیں اور فرض کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوئی اس لئے اگر چار شوط سے پہلے جماع کر لیا تو عمرہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سات شوط طواف عمرہ میں فرض ہیں اس لئے اس کی قضا لازم ہوگی۔ اور عمرہ چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے بکری لازم ہوگی ۔ بکری لازم ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عمرہ حج سے کم درجہ کا ہے اس لئے کم درجہ کا دم لازم ہوگا۔ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَهَلَّ هُوَ وَامْرَأَتُهُ جَمِيعًا بِعُمْرَةٍ فَقَضَتْ مَنَاسِكَهَا إِلَّا التَّقْصِيرَ فَغَشِيَهَا قَبْلَ أَنْ تُقَصِّرَ فَسُئِلَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ عَنْ ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ إِنَّهَا لَشَبِقَةٌ ... وَقَالَ لَهَا أَهْرِيقِي دَمًا قَالَتْ مَاذَا قَالَ انْحَرِي نَاقَةً أَوْ بَقَرَةً أَوْ شَاةً قَالَتْ أَيَّ ذَلِكَ أَفْضَلُ قَالَ نَاقَةً (ب) (سن للبیھقی ، باب المعتمر لا يقرب امرانت ج خامس ص ۲۸۰ نمبر ۹۸۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حلق سے ن پہلے جماع کیا تو دم لازم ہوگا ۔ اسی طرح طواف کرنے سے پہلے جماع کیا تو عمرہ فاسد ہوگا ۔ اور اس کی قضا کرنی ہوگی اور دم بھی لازم ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ جب حلق سے پہلے جماع کرنے سے دم لازم ہوا تو طواف کرنے سے پہلے بدرجہ اولی دم لازم ہوگا ۔ اور جس طرح وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے جماع کرنے سے حج فاسد ہو جاتا ہے اس طرح عمرہ میں طواف کرنے سے پہلے جماع کرنے سے عمرہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ قائدها امام شافعی کے نزدیک عمرہ فاسد ہونے میں بھی اونٹ لازم ہوگا۔ جس طرح حج فاسد ہونے میں اونٹ لازم ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اوپر کے اثر میں اونٹ کا تذکرہ ہے۔
And whoever has intercourse in Umrah before he has performed four circuits (ashwat), he has corrupted it, and he performs its qada, and upon him is a sheep. [Urdu: Whoever has intercourse in Umrah before completing four circuits of tawaf, he has invalidated the Umrah, so he continues in it and will perform its qada, and a goat is obligatory upon him. If he completes four circuits, that is the majority of the seven circuits, so it is as if the obligation has been performed. But if he does less than four circuits, it is as if he did not perform tawaf at all and the obligation is not fulfilled. Therefore, if he has intercourse before four circuits, the Umrah becomes invalid. Because the seven circuits of tawaf are fard in Umrah, so its qada is necessary. And due to leaving the Umrah, a goat is obligatory. The reason a goat is obligatory is that Umrah is of a lower rank than Hajj, so a lower penalty is required. From Sa'id ibn Jubayr: A man and his wife both entered ihram for Umrah. She completed the rites except taqsir, and he had intercourse with her before she performed taqsir. Ibn Abbas was asked about this and said: 'She is eager...' and he told her: 'Pour blood.' She asked: 'What?' He said: 'Slaughter a camel, or a cow, or a sheep.' She asked: 'Which is best?' He said: 'A camel.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, 986) This athar indicates that if intercourse occurs before halq, a dam is required. Similarly, if intercourse occurs before tawaf, the Umrah is invalid, requiring qada and a dam. Since even before halq a dam is required, before tawaf it is even more deserving (awla). And just as pre-wuquf intercourse invalidates Hajj, pre-tawaf intercourse invalidates Umrah. Benefit: Imam Shafi'i holds that for invalidated Umrah, a camel is required, as in Hajj, because the hadith mentions a camel.]
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that if a person has intercourse during Umrah before completing four circuits of tawaf, the Umrah is invalidated, he must continue and complete it (and later perform qada), and a sheep is owed as penalty. The author explains that four circuits constitute the majority of tawaf; less than that means tawaf is not effectively performed, so intercourse before that threshold invalidates Umrah. The penalty is a sheep because Umrah is lesser than Hajj. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas regarding a woman who had intercourse before taqsir (which is after tawaf), but the author uses qiyas (analogy) to argue that before tawaf it is even more serious. The distinction with Shafi'i is noted: Shafi'i requires a camel for invalidated Umrah, comparable to Hajj.

Key Terms
عمرة (umrah): The lesser pilgrimage consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'i, and halq/taqsir.
قضاء (qada): Making up an invalidated or missed act of worship; here it means performing a complete Umrah again after invalidation.
شاة (shah): A sheep or goat, used as the sacrificial animal for penalties (dam) in Umrah and Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person has intercourse during Umrah before completing four circuits of tawaf?
A) The Umrah is still valid and no penalty is required.
B) The Umrah is invalid, qada is required, and a sheep must be sacrificed.
C) The Umrah is invalid, qada is required, and a camel must be sacrificed.
D) He must leave the state of ihram immediately and perform no further acts.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse before completing four circuits of tawaf in Umrah invalidates it, requiring qada and the sacrifice of a sheep; Shafi'is require a camel.

Intercourse After Four Tawaf Circuits in Umrah
Ruling on post-four circuits intercourse in Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intercourse after four circuits of tawaf in Umrah and explain why the Umrah remains valid.

Core Idea
Intercourse after four tawaf circuits incurs a penalty but does not invalidate Umrah.

In the previous lesson, we learned that intercourse before completing four circuits invalidates Umrah and requires qada. Here we encounter the opposite scenario: after four circuits, the Umrah remains valid. Why? Because the majority of tawaf (four out of seven circuits) constitutes completion of the essential part. However, a penalty is still due for violating the ihram before full release. This ruling balances the sanctity of ihram with the principle that an act is considered valid once its majority is performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is intercourse (wat') during Umrah, and the timing is after completing four circuits of tawaf. Note: tawaf consists of seven circuits, so four is more than half (majority).
The threshold of four circuits is key; before four, the ruling is different.
2
State the two-part ruling
First, the Umrah is valid (sahih) and no qada (repetition) is required. Second, a penalty of one sheep (shah) is obligatory due to the violation of ihram.
The penalty is wajib, not fard, and the Umrah itself is not invalidated.
3
Explain the legal basis
In Hanafi fiqh, once the majority (ghalabah) of the essential acts of a ritual is performed, the ritual is considered effectively complete for validity, though penalties for violations remain. Four of seven circuits is the majority, so the Umrah stands.
This is based on the principle that 'the majority takes the rule of the whole' (al-ghalabah bi-manzilat al-kull).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَانْ وَطِيَ بَعْدَ مَا طَافَ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ (۱۸) اور اگر عمرہ میں چار شوط طواف کرنے کے بعد جماع کیا تو اس پر بکری لازم ہے اور اس کا عمرہ فاسد نہیں ہوگا اور نہ اس کی قضا لازم ہوگی۔
And if he has intercourse after he has performed four circuits, upon him is a sheep. (18) [Urdu: And if in Umrah, after performing four circuits of tawaf, he has intercourse, then a goat is obligatory upon him, but his Umrah will not be invalid, nor will qada be required.]
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It provides the converse of the previous lesson: if a person has intercourse in Umrah after completing four circuits of tawaf, the Umrah remains valid (because the majority of tawaf has been performed), but he still incurs a penalty of a sheep. Since the tawaf is essentially complete (four out of seven circuits constitute the majority), the Umrah is not invalidated, and no qada is required. However, the act of intercourse before the full release from ihram (which occurs after sa'y and halq/taqsir) is still a violation warranting a penalty. The penalty is a sheep, lighter than the camel for Hajj violations, consistent with the lower status of Umrah.

Key Terms
وطء (wat'): Intercourse; in this context, it is synonymous with 'jama'a'.
شاة (shah): A sheep or goat; the animal required as a penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has intercourse after completing four circuits of tawaf in Umrah, what is the ruling?
A) The Umrah is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The Umrah is valid but a sheep must be sacrificed.
C) The Umrah is valid and no penalty is required.
D) The Umrah is valid but a camel must be sacrificed.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after four tawaf circuits in Umrah does not invalidate the Umrah but requires a sheep as penalty.

Intercourse in Umrah: Rulings, Proofs, and Disputes
Rulings with proofs on intercourse in Umrah and related penalties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on intercourse before and after four rounds of tawaf in Umrah, explain the distinction between invalidating and non-invalidating intercourse, identify the proof from the athar, and evaluate the Shafi'i disagreement.

Core Idea
Intercourse before four tawaf rounds invalidates Umrah; after four rounds, only a sheep is due – the pillar is already fulfilled.

In Umrah, the point at which intercourse occurs determines whether the pilgrimage is invalidated or merely requires a penalty. The Hanafi school, following the athar of Ibn Abbas, distinguishes between intercourse before and after completing most of the obligatory tawaf. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and the Shafi'i counter-argument, as well as related rulings on forgetful intercourse and tawaf al-qudum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read rulings (17) and (18): intercourse before four rounds invalidates Umrah; after four rounds, Umrah remains valid but a sheep is due. Understand the difference in outcome.
The threshold is four rounds, which is more than half of seven.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Study the athar of Ibn Abbas (and Sa'id ibn Jubayr) cited in the passage. Note the phrase 'يعتمر ويهدى' – he performs Umrah (repeats) and offers a hadi. Understand how this is interpreted as a sheep due to Umrah's lower rank.
The proof is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school holds that any intercourse before sa'y invalidates Umrah, even after four tawaf rounds. Their proof is the hadith of Jabir: 'لا يقربنها حتى يطوف بين الصفا والمروة'.
The dispute hinges on whether sa'y is a pillar (rukn) or wajib.
4
Note additional rulings
Ruling (19) equates forgetful intercourse with intentional, citing general texts and the principle of benefit. Ruling (20) requires sadaqah for performing tawaf al-qudum in a state of minor impurity (hadath).
These rulings have their own proofs and intra-school discussions.

کر اور بھول کر کرنے میں فرق نہیں کیا گیا ہے اس لئے دونوں کے احکام ایک ہوں گے۔ صرف روزے میں بھول کر کرنے سے کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ وہاں اس کی تصریح کر دی گئی ہے (۲) حج اور عمرہ کی حالت یاد دلانے والی ہے الحسن وعطاء انهما قالا في ثلاث شعرات دم الناسي والمعتمد فيها سواء سن البیهقی ، باب الحرم لا تحلق شعره ج خامس ص ۹۸ نمبر ۹۱۲۴ دارقطنی نمبر ۲۵۱۲) ان اثر میں بھول اور جان کر جنایت کرنے کو برا بر قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ نانه امام شافعی کے نزدیک بھول کر کرنے سے جنایت لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ ان کے نزدیک بھول سے کچھ لازم نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ امت سے خطا اور نسیان معاف کر دیا گیا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل او پر گزر چکی ہے۔ [۷۳۳] (۲۰) جس نے طواف قدوم محدث ہو کر کیا تو اس پر صدقہ ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے جابر بن عبد اللہ سے پوچھا تو فرمایا کہ عورت کے قریب نہ جائے جب تک کہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی نہ کرلے۔
(730) (17) Whoever has intercourse in Umrah before completing four rounds of tawaf, he invalidates it, proceeds in it, and makes it up, and upon him is a sheep. (18) And if he has intercourse after completing four rounds of tawaf, upon him is a sheep, and his Umrah is not invalidated, nor is its repetition required. In the athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas there is an indication of this: from Ibn Abbas that he said concerning one who has intercourse with his wife before ifada (the tawaf of ziyara): he performs Umrah and offers a hadi. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) In this athar, hadi is absolute, so it can be said that if he has intercourse after shaving and before tawaf al-ziyara, then the absolute hadi means a sheep. (730) (17) Whoever has intercourse in Umrah before having performed four rounds of tawaf, he has invalidated his Umrah, so he continues in it, repeats it, and upon him is a sheep. If he has performed four rounds, that is more than half of seven, so it is as if he has performed the obligatory part. But if he has performed less than four rounds, it is as if he has not done tawaf at all and the obligation is not fulfilled. Therefore, if he has intercourse before four rounds, his Umrah is invalidated because seven rounds of tawaf are obligatory in Umrah. So he must repeat it, and due to abandoning the Umrah, a sheep is necessary. The reason for the sheep is that Umrah is of a lower degree than Hajj, so a lower degree of dam is necessary. From Sa'id ibn Jubayr: A man and his wife both entered into ihram for Umrah, and she performed all the rites except taqsir, then he had intercourse with her before she performed taqsir. Ibn Abbas was asked about that, and he said: She hastened... and he said to her: Shed blood. She said: What? He said: Slaughter a camel or a cow or a sheep. She said: Which is best? He said: A camel. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) In this athar, if he has intercourse before shaving, dam is necessary. Similarly, if he has intercourse before tawaf, Umrah is invalidated, and he must repeat it and pay dam. Because when intercourse before shaving necessitates dam, then before tawaf it is even more deserving. And just as intercourse before standing at Arafah invalidates Hajj, so intercourse before tawaf in Umrah invalidates Umrah. According to Imam Shafi'i, in the invalidation of Umrah, a camel is necessary, just as in the invalidation of Hajj a camel is necessary because the above athar mentions a camel. (731) (18) And if he has intercourse in Umrah after completing four rounds of tawaf, upon him is a sheep, and his Umrah is not invalidated, nor is its repetition required. Footnote (a): Ibn Abbas said about a man who has intercourse before tawaf al-ziyara: he performs Umrah and offers a hadi. (b) Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: A man and his wife declared ihram for Umrah, then she performed all rites except taqsir, then he had intercourse with her before taqsir. Ibn Abbas was asked and said: She hastened... and said to her: Shed blood. She said: What? He said: Slaughter a camel or a cow or a sheep. She said: Which is best? He said: A camel. [PAGE_451] (732) (19) And whoever has intercourse forgetfully, is like one who does it intentionally in the ruling. (733) (20) And whoever performs tawaf al-qudum while in a state of hadath, upon him is sadaqah. In Umrah, seven rounds of tawaf are obligatory. However, sa'y between Safa and Marwah is not obligatory according to the Hanafis; it is wajib. Therefore, if one has completed four rounds, which is more than half of seven, it is as if he has performed the pillar of tawaf in Umrah, so Umrah is not invalidated. But sa'y and shaving remain, and he has had intercourse, so dam is necessary. The above hadith provides proof. According to Imam Shafi'i, if one has intercourse after four rounds of tawaf, Umrah is still invalidated. Their evidence is this athar: We asked Jabir ibn Abdullah, and he said: 'He should not approach her until he runs between Safa and Marwah.' (Sahih al-Bukhari) This athar shows that he should not have intercourse before sa'y, and if he did, it is as if he abandoned an obligation, so Umrah is invalidated. (732) (19) Whoever has intercourse forgetfully, his ruling is like that of one who does it intentionally. The same penalties apply in Hajj and Umrah whether done forgetfully or intentionally. (1) The general texts do not differentiate between intentional and forgetful, so the rulings are the same. Only in fasting does one who forgets not incur kaffarah; that is specified. (2) The state of Hajj and Umrah is a reminder, so forgetfulness is not considered in them. (3) In these, the basis of the violation is the attainment of benefit, and benefit is attained whether done forgetfully, so dam is necessary. There is an athar for this: Malik said: ... or he shaves the back of his head at the place of cupping while in ihram forgetfully or ignorantly: whoever does any of these, upon him is the fidyah in all cases. (Muwatta) From al-Hasan and Ata: they said concerning three hairs: blood is due from the forgetful and the intentional equally. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This athar equates forgetful and intentional violations. According to Imam Shafi'i, forgetful violations do not incur penalties because the ummah is forgiven for error and forgetfulness. His proof has preceded. (733) (20) Whoever performs tawaf al-qudum while in a state of hadath, upon him is sadaqah. Footnote (a): I asked Jabir ibn Abdullah, and he said: 'He should not approach her until he runs between Safa and Marwah.'
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage from al-Sharh al-Thamiri covers several rulings regarding sexual intercourse during Umrah and Hajj. The author begins with the ruling (17): if one has intercourse in Umrah before completing four rounds of tawaf, the Umrah is invalidated (fasid). The person must continue in the state and then repeat the Umrah (qada), and also sacrifice a sheep (shah). The reason is that four rounds constitute more than half of the obligatory seven rounds, so performing less than four means the tawaf is not considered done at all, akin to omitting a pillar (rukn). The proof is from the athar of Ibn Abbas where he says the one who has intercourse before tawaf al-ziyara must perform Umrah and offer a hadi. The author clarifies that 'hadi' in that context means a sheep, as Umrah is of lower rank than Hajj. A second athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr reinforces that intercourse before taqsir (hair cutting) necessitates dam, and by qiyas, before tawaf it is even more severe. The Hanafi position is that before four rounds, Umrah is invalid; after four rounds, only a dam is due. The author then contrasts with Imam Shafi'i, who holds that any intercourse before sa'y (between Safa and Marwah) invalidates Umrah, citing the hadith of Jabir. In ruling (18), after four rounds, the Umrah remains valid but a sheep is due. The Hanafi reasoning: since more than half of the obligatory tawaf is done, the pillar is considered fulfilled. The remaining sa'y and shaving are not pillars (they are wajib according to Hanafis), so intercourse does not nullify the Umrah. Ruling (19) addresses forgetful intercourse: the Hanafi position is that it is treated the same as intentional, because general texts do not distinguish and the situation of Hajj/Umrah is a reminder. Also, the benefit is attained anyway. Evidence is from Malik and from al-Hasan and Ata equating forgetful and intentional in shaving hair. Shafi'i disagrees, citing the general principle of forgiveness for error. Ruling (20) covers tawaf al-qudum while in a state of hadath (minor ritual impurity). The Hanafi ruling is that sadaqah (charity) is due, but the nature and amount are not specified here; it implies the tawaf is still valid but a penalty applies.

Key Terms
عمرة (umrah): The lesser pilgrimage, consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq or taqsir.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba; in Umrah, seven rounds are obligatory (fard).
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as penalty for violating the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person has intercourse in Umrah after completing four rounds of tawaf but before sa'y?
A) The Umrah is invalid and must be repeated with a camel.
B) The Umrah is valid but a sheep must be sacrificed.
C) The Umrah is valid and no penalty is required.
D) The Umrah is invalid and must be repeated with a sheep.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intercourse before completing four rounds of tawaf in Umrah invalidates the pilgrimage; after four rounds, only a penalty sheep is due, as the tawaf pillar is considered fulfilled.

Intentional and Forgetful Intercourse in Ihram: Same Ruling
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetful intercourse during ihram and explain why it is not excused, citing the dalil and distinguishing the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Forgetful intercourse in ihram requires the same dam as intentional—forgetfulness does not excuse the violation.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samiri presents a clear Hanafi position: forgetfulness does not exempt a pilgrim from the penalty of intercourse during ihram. The author provides three rationales and cites an athar from the Muwatta to support the ruling. The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that forgetfulness is generally excused. Understanding this ruling is crucial for anyone advising pilgrims or studying the distinctiveness of Hanafi fiqh in Hajj matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (forgetful intercourse in ihram). What is the hukm? (the same dam as intentional intercourse is required).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? (an athar from Malik's Muwatta about a muhrim shaving forgetfully, and a statement from al-Hasan and Ata).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the athar prove the ruling? It explicitly says fidyah is due whether one acts forgetfully or ignorantly.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Which school disagrees and on what basis? The Shafi'i school holds that forgetfulness absolves penalties due to the hadith of forgiveness for error and forgetfulness.

(732) (19) And whoever has intercourse forgetfully, is like one who does it intentionally in the ruling. The one who has intercourse forgetfully, his ruling is like that of one who does it intentionally. The same penalties apply in Hajj and Umrah whether done forgetfully or intentionally. (1) The general texts do not differentiate between intentional and forgetful, so the rulings are the same. Only in fasting does one who forgets not incur kaffarah; that is specified. (2) The state of Hajj and Umrah is a reminder, so forgetfulness is not considered in them. (3) In these, the basis of the violation is the attainment of benefit, and benefit is attained whether done forgetfully, so dam is necessary. There is an athar for this: Malik said: ... or he shaves the back of his head at the place of cupping while in ihram forgetfully or ignorantly: whoever does any of these, upon him is the fidyah in all cases. (Muwatta) From al-Hasan and Ata: they said concerning three hairs: blood is due from the forgetful and the intentional equally. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This athar equates forgetful and intentional violations. According to Imam Shafi'i, forgetful violations do not incur penalties because the ummah is forgiven for error and forgetfulness. His proof has preceded.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This short ruling (19) establishes the Hanafi position on forgetful intercourse during ihram: it is treated exactly like intentional intercourse, requiring the same dam (blood sacrifice). The author provides three justifications. First, the general texts (nusus) do not distinguish between intentional and forgetful acts; only in fasting is forgetfulness excused from kaffarah, which is an exception. Second, the state of ihram is a constant reminder, so forgetfulness is not a valid excuse. Third, the essence of the violation (jinaya) is the attainment of benefit (irtifaq), and benefit is obtained whether one remembers or forgets. The author then cites an athar from Imam Malik in the Muwatta: if a muhrim shaves the back of his head (for cupping) forgetfully or ignorantly, fidyah is due. Another athar from al-Hasan and Ata says that for removing three hairs, blood (dam) is due from both the forgetful and the intentional. Finally, the author mentions the Shafi'i counter-position: forgetfulness absolves penalties based on the hadith of forgiveness for error and forgetfulness. The Hanafi response is implicit: the specific proof for ihram violations overrides the general principle.

Key Terms
ناسی (nasi): One who forgets; in this context, a person who commits a violation of ihram without intending to.
جنایت (jinaya): A violation of the prohibitions of ihram that incurs a penalty (dam or sadaqah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is forgetful intercourse in ihram not excused?
A) Because the texts specifically mention forgetfulness as an exception.
B) Because the state of ihram is a constant reminder and forgetfulness is thus not plausible.
C) Because the Qur'an says intentional and forgetful are the same.
D) Because the Sahaba unanimously ruled so.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness does not excuse from penalties in Hajj/Umrah violations according to Hanafi; the same dam is due as for intentional acts.

Tawaf al-Qudum without Wudu Requires Sadaqah
Ruling on tawaf al-qudum without wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for performing tawaf al-qudum without wudu and identify the compensatory obligation.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-qudum without wudu requires sadaqah but the tawaf itself remains valid.

We now encounter a specific ruling on the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) in Hajj. The passage states that performing this tawaf without wudu (in a state of hadath) obligates a sadaqah. This lesson clarifies the ruling and why compensation is needed even though the tawaf is still valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is tawaf al-qudum performed in a state of hadath. The ruling: upon him is sadaqah (charity).
The text does not specify the amount; Hanafi fiqh specifies half a sa' of wheat or its value.
2
Identify the omitted condition
The condition of taharah (wudu) was omitted. In Hanafi, taharah for tawaf al-qudum is wajib, not fard.
This distinction is key: wajib omission requires compensation but does not invalidate.
3
State the consequence
The tawaf is valid (sahih) but makruh, and sadaqah is obligatory to compensate for the omitted wajib.
This differs from tawaf al-ifadah where taharah is a condition of validity.
4
Memorize the ruling
Commit to memory: 'Whoever performs tawaf al-qudum in a state of hadath must give sadaqah.'
This is a concise matn statement from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۷۳۳ (۲۰) ومن طاف طواف القدوم محدثا فعليه صدقة . جس نے طواف قدوم محدث ہو کر کیا تو اس پر صدقہ ہے۔
(733) (20) And whoever performs tawaf al-qudum while in a state of hadath, upon him is sadaqah. The one who performs tawaf al-qudum while in a state of hadath, upon him is sadaqah (charity).
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This is a concise ruling stating that if a pilgrim performs the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) without being in a state of ritual purity (i.e., without wudu, having hadath), he must give sadaqah (charity). The amount of sadaqah is not specified here but according to Hanafi fiqh, it is half a sa' of wheat or its value. The tawaf itself is considered valid but makruh, and the sadaqah compensates for the omission of a required condition (taharah for tawaf is wajib according to Hanafis). This differs from the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ifadah/ziyarah) where taharah is a condition for validity.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca by a pilgrim performing Hajj, known as the arrival tawaf.
محدث (muhdith): A person in a state of ritual impurity (hadath) that requires wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What penalty is due for performing tawaf al-qudum while in a state of hadath, according to this passage?
A) A sheep (dam).
B) Sadaqah (charity).
C) Nothing; the tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
D) A camel.

Key Takeaway
Performing tawaf al-qudum without wudu is valid but requires sadaqah (charity) as compensation for omitting the wajib condition of taharah.
