Ruling on Tawaf Qudum with Janabah
Ruling and proof for penalty when performing Tawaf Qudum in major impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the penalty for Tawaf Qudum performed without wudu (hadath) and in janabah, and explain why the Hanafi school considers the tawaf valid despite impurity.

Core Idea
Tawaf without wudu is valid but requires sadaqah; janabah requires a sheep.

In this passage, the author discusses Tawaf Qudum, the arrival tawaf in Makkah. The ideal is to perform it with wudu. However, what happens if one performs it without wudu or in a state of major impurity (janabah)? The Hanafi school rules that the tawaf is still valid, but a compensatory penalty is required: sadaqah for minor impurity, and a sheep for janabah. This lesson unpacks the evidence from hadith and Quran that leads to this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that Tawaf Qudum is a sunnah act that ideally requires wudu. The ruling on performing it without wudu is that it is valid but carries a penalty.
The act itself is not invalidated; only compensation is required.
2
Distinguish the penalties
Note that hadath (minor impurity) incurs sadaqah (half sa' of wheat), while janabah (major impurity) incurs a sheep. The difference is due to the severity of deficiency.
Janabah is considered a greater deficiency because it requires ghusl.
3
Analyze the proof from the hadith 'tawaf is like prayer'
Examine the hadith from Ibn Abbas that states 'tawaf around the House is like prayer except that you speak during it.' This hadith is used to argue that purification is a condition for tawaf.
The Hanafi school interprets this as establishing a meritorious requirement, not absolute validity.
4
Resolve the apparent conflict with the Quranic verse
The Quranic verse (22:29) commands tawaf without mentioning purity. The Hanafi school gives priority to this general command, allowing the tawaf to be valid even without wudu, but the hadith imposes a penalty for the deficiency.
This prioritization is a key usul principle: the Quranic 'amm' is not restricted by a solitary hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
۷۳۴ (۲۱) وان كان جنبا فعليه شاة [۷۳۵ (۲۲) وان طاف طواف الزيارة محدثا فعليه
طواف قدوم وضو کی حالت میں کرنا چاہئے لیکن کسی نے حدث کی حالت میں طواف قدوم کر لیا تو اس پر صدقہ لازم ہوگا۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے اور نماز میں وضو ضروری ہے اس لئے طواف میں بھی وضو ضروری ہوگا۔ اس لئے اگر بغیر وضو کے طواف قدوم کیا تو صدقہ لازم ہوگا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس ان النبى الله الله قال الطواف حول البيت مثل الصلوة الا انكم تتكلمون فيه فمن تكلم فيه فلا يتكلم الا بخير (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الکلام فی الطواف ص ۱۹۰ حدیث نمبر ۹۶۰ نسائی شریف ، باب اباحۃ الکلام فی الطواف ج ثانی ص ۲۸ نمبر ۲۹۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے اس لئے طواف میں بھی وضو شرط ہے (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة انها قالت قدمت مكة وانا حائض ولم اطف بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة قالت فشكوت ذلك الى رسول الله فقال افعلى كما يفعل الحاج غير ان لا تطوفي بالبيت حتى تطهری (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب تقصی الحائض المناسک کلھا الا الطواف بالبيت ص ۲۲۳ نمبر ۱۶۵۰) اس حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلا کہ طہارت کے بغیر طواف نہ کرے۔ تاہم طواف کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ قرآن نے جو طواف کا تذکرہ کیا ہے اس میں طہارت کی شرط نہیں لگائی ہے اس لئے بغیر وضو کے طواف کیا تو طواف ادا ہو جائے گا۔ آیت ہے وليطوفوا بالبيت العتيق (آیت ۲۹ سورة الحج ۲۲) اس آیت میں طواف کرنے کا حکم دیا لیکن طہارت کی شرط نہیں لگائی اس لئے بغیر طہارت کے بھی طواف ہو جائے گا البتہ صدقہ یا دم لازم ہوگا۔
صدقہ سے مراد صدقۃ الفطر کی مقدار آدھا صاع ہے۔ کیونکہ مطلق صدقہ سے صدقۃ الفطر کی مقدار مراد ہوتی ہے۔
[۷۳۴] (۲۱) اور اگر طواف قدوم جنبی ہو کر کر لیا تو اس پر بکری لازم ہے۔ جنابت کی حالت میں طواف قدوم کیا تو طواف میں حدث کی بنسبت زیادہ نقص ہوا اس لئے بکری لازم ہوگی۔ باقی وجہ مسئلہ نمبر ۲۰ میں گزر چکی (۲) دم لازم ہونے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے ان عبد الله بن عباس قال مـن نسـى مـن نـســکـه شيئا او تركه فليهرق دما (الف) (موطا امام مالک ، باب ما يفعل من نسی من نسکه شیبا ص ۲۵۰ سفن البیهقی ، باب من ترک هیما من الرمی حتی يذهب ایام منی ، ج خامس، ص ۱۵۲ار دار قطنی، ج ثانی ص ۲۱۵ نمبر ۲۵۱۴/۲۵۱۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کچھ چھوٹ جائے تو دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور جنابت کی حالت میں طواف کرنا سے گویا کہ طواف چھوٹ گیا اس لئے دم لازم ہوگا۔
Book of Hajj. 734 (21): If he was in a state of janabah, then upon him is a sheep. [735 (22): And if he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of hadath, then upon him...] Tawaf Qudum should be done in a state of wudu. But if someone performed Tawaf Qudum in a state of hadath, then sadaqah becomes obligatory upon him. The hadith states that tawaf around the House is like prayer, and in prayer wudu is necessary, so wudu is necessary in tawaf. Therefore, if he performed Tawaf Qudum without wudu, sadaqah becomes obligatory. There is a hadith: From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer except that you speak during it, so whoever speaks should only speak good.' (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) This hadith shows that tawaf is like prayer, so wudu is a condition in tawaf. (2) Another hadith: From Aisha that she said: I came to Makkah while menstruating and did not perform tawaf around the House nor between Safa and Marwah. She complained to the Messenger of Allah, and he said: 'Do as the pilgrim does, except do not perform tawaf around the House until you are pure.' (Bukhari) This hadith also shows that one should not perform tawaf without purification. However, the tawaf will be valid (adā'). Because the Quran mentions tawaf without stipulating purification. So if he performed tawaf without wudu, the tawaf is valid (adā'), but sadaqah or a sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory. Sadaqah refers to the quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr, which is half a sa'. Because absolute sadaqah means the quantity of Sadaqat al-Fitr. [734] (21) And if he performed Tawaf Qudum in a state of janabah, then upon him is a sheep. Because performing Tawaf Qudum in janabah is a greater deficiency than in hadath, so a sheep is obliged. The rest of the reason has passed in issue no. 20. The proof for the obligation of dam is the athar: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him shed blood (i.e., offer a sacrifice).' (Muwatta Malik, Bayhaqi, Dar Qutni) This athar indicates that if something is missed, dam becomes obligatory. And performing tawaf in janabah is as if the tawaf was missed, so dam is obligatory.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs concerning Tawaf Qudum (the arrival tawaf) performed without wudu or in a state of major impurity (janabah). The author first establishes that Tawaf Qudum should ideally be done with wudu. If done without wudu (minor impurity), sadaqah (a charity of half a sa' of wheat) is required. If done in janabah (major impurity), a sheep (shah) is required. This is because janabah is a greater deficiency than hadath. The author provides two hadith proofs: the famous hadith that 'tawaf around the House is like prayer' (from Ibn Abbas) establishes that purification is a condition for tawaf, as it is for prayer. The hadith of Aisha shows that a menstruating woman must avoid tawaf until purification, implying that tawaf without purification is deficient. However, relying on the Quranic verse 'and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House' (Quran 22:29), which does not explicitly require purification, the author argues that the tawaf is still valid (adā' al-adā') but entails a compensatory penalty. For hadath, the penalty is sadaqah; for janabah, it is a sheep. The author also cites an athar from Ibn Abbas that any omission from the rites requires blood (dam), which is used as a general principle for missed obligations in Hajj. The commentary follows the matn order, first stating the ideal, then the ruling for impurity, and finally the proofs.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Makkah as a greeting to the Sacred Mosque.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable payment of half a sa' of wheat (or equivalent) as determined by Sadaqat al-Fitr standard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the penalty for performing Tawaf Qudum in a state of janabah (major impurity)?
A) Sadaqah of half a sa'
B) A sheep (shah)
C) Nothing, the tawaf is invalid and must be repeated
D) A camel (badanah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely holds that tawaf without purity is valid but requires a compensatory penalty: sadaqah for hadath, a sheep for janabah.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah Performed with Hadath
Ruling with justification for Tawaf al-Ziyarah with hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed in a state of minor impurity and explain why a sheep is required as compensation.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah without wudu is valid but deficient; compensation by sacrificing a sheep.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hajj: what happens if a pilgrim performs the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of minor impurity (hadath). The Hanafi school holds that the tawaf remains valid, but due to the deficiency caused by missing the recommended purity, a penalty is required. Understanding this ruling illuminates the Hanafi distinction between pillars (arkan) and obligatory elements (wajibat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the act: Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed with hadath. The ruling: the tawaf is valid, but a sheep (shah) is obligatory.
The act is a fard pillar of Hajj.
2
Understand the legal reason (ta'lil)
The author explains that because Tawaf al-Ziyarah is fard and 'important,' performing it without purity leaves a deficiency (naqs). This deficiency must be compensated by an animal sacrifice.
The penalty is higher than for Tawaf Qudum (which requires sadaqah) due to the elevated status of Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
3
Differentiate from other tawafs
Compare with Tawaf Qudum: for that tawaf, performing it with hadath requires only sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat). Here, the penalty is a full sheep because Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a fard pillar.
This distinction shows how the level of obligation affects the required compensation.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
In Hanafi fiqh, purity (taharah) is not a condition (shart) for the validity of tawaf, but a wajib (obligatory element) whose omission is compensated. This principle explains why the tawaf is not invalidated.
Contrast with the Shafi'i school, which considers purity a condition, making the tawaf invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۳۵] (۲۲) اور اگر طواف زیارت محدث ہو کر کیا تو اس پر بکری لازم ہے۔
چونکہ طواف زیارت اہم ہے اور فرض ہے اور اس کو محدث ہو کر کر لیا تو کمی رہی اس لئے اس کمی کو بکری ذبح کر کے پوری کرے۔
[735] (22) And if he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of hadath (minor impurity), then upon him is a sheep (shah). Because Tawaf al-Ziyarah is important and is fard (obligatory), and he performed it in a state of hadath, so there is a deficiency. Therefore, he should compensate this deficiency by slaughtering a sheep.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This is a concise ruling regarding Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the essential tawaf of Hajj). The author states that if one performs this tawaf without wudu (minor impurity), a sheep (shah) is obligatory as compensation. The reason given is that this tawaf is 'important and farḍ' — it is a fundamental pillar of Hajj. Performing it in a state of impurity leaves a deficiency (naqṣ) in the rite, which must be remedied by offering a sheep. The ruling is simpler than for Tawaf Qudum, where hadath required only sadaqah; here, due to the higher status of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the penalty is a full animal sacrifice. The passage does not cite explicit proof here, but the general principle from earlier (Ibn Abbas athar) is implied.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj also called Tawaf al-Ifadah, performed after returning from Mina.
محدث (muhdith): A person in a state of minor impurity requiring wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What penalty applies if Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed without wudu (hadath) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sadaqah of half a sa'
B) Nothing, it is valid as is
C) A sheep (shah)
D) The tawaf must be repeated

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed without wudu valid, but the deficiency must be compensated by sacrificing a sheep.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah in Janabah: Penalty and Preferred Action
Ruling for Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed in major impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed in janabah and explain the distinction between the obligatory penalty (badanah) and the preferred repetition.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah requires a camel, but repeating the tawaf cancels the penalty.

In Hajj, Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a pillar of the pilgrimage. Performing it while in a state of janabah (major impurity) creates a deficiency. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling: the act is valid but deficient, requiring either a camel sacrifice or, preferably, a repetition of the tawaf. Understanding this helps avoid unnecessary penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah. According to the Hanafi school, the tawaf is valid but deficient, and a penalty (camel) is wajib.
This is a case of a fard act performed with a missing condition.
2
State the penalty and its severity
The penalty is a badanah (camel). The text explains that janabah is a 'great crime' requiring a greater penalty than a sheep (which is for minor hadath).
The severity reflects the deficiency's magnitude.
3
Identify the preferred action
The afḍal (better) course is to repeat the tawaf while still in Makkah. Repetition makes up for the deficiency, so no slaughter is due.
Repetition is recommended but not obligatory; the camel is only due if he does not repeat.
4
Understand the rationale
Repetition is like 'making up for the deficiency' – it repairs the imperfect tawaf. This is a Hanafi principle of allowing compensation for missing conditions.
Other schools may consider the tawaf invalid; Hanafi uses istihsan.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds tawaf invalid without purity, so repetition is mandatory and no penalty substitutes. Hanafi allows a penalty as an alternative.
Knowing this difference is useful for practical issues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۳۶] (۲۳) وان كان جنبا فعليه بدنة والافضل ان يعيد الطواف مادام بمكة ولا ذبح علیه
[۷۳۶] (۲۳) اور اگر طواف زیارت جنبی ہو کر کرلیا تو اس پر اونٹ لازم ہے۔ اور افضل یہ ہے کہ طواف کولوٹا لے جب تک مکہ میں رہے۔ پھر اس پر ذبح نہیں ہے۔
اگر طواف لوٹایا تو دم لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جس میں نقص تھا اس کو پورا کر لیا اس لئے دم لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور افضل یہی ہے کہ ایسے نقص والے طواف کو دوبارہ کر لے۔
طواف زیارت کو جنبی ہو کر کیا تو یہ بڑی جنایت ہے اس لئے اس میں دم بھی بڑا یعنی اونٹ لا زم ہوگا۔
[736] (23) And if he was in a state of janabah, then upon him is a camel (badanah), and the better (afḍal) is to repeat the tawaf as long as he is in Makkah, and then no slaughter is upon him. [736] (23) And if he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah, then a camel is obligatory upon him. And the better is to repeat the tawaf while he is in Makkah. Then there is no slaughter on him. If he repeats the tawaf, then dam is not obligatory. Because he has made up the deficiency, so dam is not obligatory. And the better is to repeat such a deficient tawaf. Performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah is a great crime, so the blood (dam) is also great: a camel becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage deals with Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed in a state of major impurity (janabah). The ruling is that a camel (badanah) is due—a greater penalty than the sheep for hadath because janabah is a greater deficiency. However, the preferred course (afḍal) is to repeat the tawaf while still in Makkah, which removes the obligation of any sacrifice. The reasoning is that repetition makes up for the deficiency. If he leaves Makkah without repeating, the camel is required. The severity is explained as 'a great crime', so the compensation is proportionally larger. The text emphasizes that the default is the camel, but repetition is better to avoid the penalty.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel (or cow) sacrificed as a penalty in Hajj; here specifically a camel.
افضل (afḍal): The preferred or better option, not obligatory but recommended to remove the deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred action (afḍal) for someone who performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah?
A) Slaughter a camel immediately
B) Repeat the tawaf while still in Makkah
C) Make a vow to sacrifice on behalf of the deficiency
D) Do nothing, as the tawaf is valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows a deficient tawaf to be remedied either by penalty or repetition, with repetition being the preferred option to avoid the camel.

Penalties for Tawaf al-Sudr with Impurity
Penalties for Tawaf al-Sudr with impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the penalty for Tawaf al-Sudr when performed with hadath or janabah and explain why it differs from Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sudr with impurity is valid but costly: sadaqah for hadath, sheep for janabah.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Sudr (Farewell Tawaf) when performed without purification. Unlike the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which requires a full sacrifice (dam) if done in impurity, Tawaf al-Sudr is considered a lesser tawaf and carries a lighter penalty: sadaqah for minor impurity (hadath) and a sheep for major impurity (janabah). The ruling is analogous to Tawaf Qudum (Arrival Tawaf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
Recognize that Tawaf al-Sudr is a wajib act of Hajj, not fard. It is performed before departing Makkah.
Hanafi: Tawaf al-Sudr is wajib; Shafi'i considers it fard.
2
Differentiate the two impurity cases
Note the two states: hadath (minor impurity, e.g. lacking wudu) and janabah (major impurity, e.g. after intercourse). Each triggers a different penalty.
The penalty for janabah is greater due to the severity of the transgression.
3
State the penalties
For hadath: sadaqah (charity of half a sa' of wheat or equivalent). For janabah: a sheep (shah).
Sadaqah is a smaller penalty; a sheep is more substantial.
4
Understand the analogy to Tawaf Qudum
The commentator explains that Tawaf al-Sudr is of lower rank than Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so its ruling mirrors Tawaf Qudum (the arrival tawaf), not the obligatory one.
This analogy helps explain why the penalty is lighter.
5
Distinguish from Tawaf al-Ziyarah
For Tawaf al-Ziyarah (fard), impurity invalidates the tawaf and requires a dam (sacrifice). For Tawaf al-Sudr, the tawaf is valid but carries a penalty.
This distinction is critical for correct fiqh application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۳۷] (۲۴) ومن طاف طواف الصدر محدثا فعليه صدقة وان كان جنبا فعليه شاة
[۷۳۷] (۲۴) جس نے طواف وداع حدث کی حالت میں کیا اس پر صدقہ ہے اور اگر جنابت کی حالت میں کیا تو اس پر بکری ہے۔ طواف وداع طواف زیارت سے کم درجہ ہے اس لئے اس کا حکم طواف قدوم کی طرح ہوگا۔ یعنی حدث کی حالت میں کیا تو صدقہ لازم ہوگا اور جنابت کی حالت میں کیا تو بکری لازم ہوگی۔ کیونکہ جنابت کی حالت میں جنایت زیادہ ہے۔
طواف صدر : طواف وداع جو آخری وقت میں کیا جاتا ہے، اس کو طواف صدر بھی کہتے ہیں۔
[737] (24) And whoever performed Tawaf al-Sudr (Farewell Tawaf) in a state of hadath, upon him is sadaqah; and if he was in a state of janabah, upon him is a sheep. [737] (24) Whoever performed Tawaf al-Wida' (Farewell Tawaf) in a state of hadath, upon him is sadaqah; and if he performed it in a state of janabah, upon him is a sheep. Tawaf al-Wida' is of a lower rank than Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so its ruling is like that of Tawaf Qudum. That is, if done in hadath, sadaqah is due; if done in janabah, a sheep is due. Because the transgression in janabah is greater. Tawaf al-Sudr: Tawaf al-Wida' performed at the end is also called Tawaf al-Sudr.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This lesson presents the ruling for Tawaf al-Sudr (Farewell Tawaf) when performed without purification. The matn states that for hadath (minor impurity), sadaqah is due; for janabah (major impurity), a sheep is due. The commentary explains that this tawaf is of a lower status than Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so its penalties mirror those of Tawaf Qudum (arrival tawaf). The rationale is that a greater impurity (janabah) constitutes a greater transgression, requiring a larger penalty. The passage also clarifies that Tawaf al-Sudr is synonymous with Tawaf al-Wida'. No explicit proof is given, but the analogy to Tawaf Qudum is drawn.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sudr): The Farewell Tawaf performed before leaving Makkah, also called Tawaf al-Wida'.
طواف الوداع (tawaf al-wida'): Same as Tawaf al-Sudr; the final circumambulation before departure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the penalty for performing Tawaf al-Sudr in a state of hadath (minor impurity)?
A) A full dam (sacrifice)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) A sheep (shah)
D) No penalty, but the tawaf is invalid

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sudr performed with hadath requires sadaqah; with janabah requires a sheep; the tawaf remains valid because it is of lower rank than the fard tawaf.

Missing Four Circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Perpetual Ihram
Hanafi ruling on incomplete Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pilgrim leaves four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and identify the consequence for his state of ihram.

Core Idea
Missing four circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah renders the tawaf void; the pilgrim remains a muhrim indefinitely until the tawaf is completed.

This lesson examines a critical scenario in Hajj: what if a pilgrim completes less than the full seven circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah? Specifically, if four or more circuits are omitted, the Hanafi school considers the tawaf as not performed at all. The consequence is severe: the pilgrim remains in the state of ihram, with all its prohibitions, including marital relations. Understanding this ruling is essential for scholars and pilgrims to emphasize the completeness of this obligatory rite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its composition
Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah) consists of seven circuits around the Kaaba. It is a pillar (rukn) of Hajj.
In Hanafi fiqh, pillars are essential; omission invalidates the act.
2
Define the threshold for invalidation
The text states that leaving four circuits (more than half of seven) means the majority is missed, so the tawaf is considered not performed at all.
Four is the threshold because it exceeds half of seven.
3
State the ruling
The pilgrim remains a muhrim forever until he performs the missing circuits. Marital relations remain forbidden.
No sacrifice or substitute can replace the tawaf; it must be performed physically.
4
Understand the rationale
Because the tawaf is a pillar, omission of the majority is equivalent to omission of the entire act. Hence the state of ihram persists.
This distinguishes it from lesser omissions that may be compensated with a sacrifice (dam).
5
Note the athar support
The text references an athar from Madinan jurists supporting that one who forgets Tawaf al-Ifadah remains in ihram.
The athar reinforces the ruling but is not the primary evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۳۹] (۲۶) وان ترک اربعة اشواط بقی محرما ابدا حتى يطوفها
[۷۳۹] (۲۶) اگر طواف زیارت میں سے چار شوط چھوڑ دیئے تو ہمیشہ محرم باقی رہے گا یہاں تک کہ طواف کرے۔ طواف زیارت میں سے چار شوط نہیں کیا تو اکثر طواف نہیں کیا تو گویا کہ طواف کیا ہی نہیں اس لئے جب تک طواف فرض نہ کرے بیوی کے بارے میں محرم ہی باقی رہے گا کیونکہ جب تک طواف زیارت نہ کرے آدمی کے لئے بیوی حلال نہیں ہوتی۔ اثر میں ہے حدثنا ابي الزناد عن الفقهاء الذين ينتهى الى قومهم من اهل المدينة كانوا يقولون من نسى ان يفيض حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس نے فرمایا جو حج کی عبادت میں سے کچھ بھول جائے یا اس کو چھوڑ دے تو اس کو خون بہانا چاہئے۔
[739] (26) And if he left four circuits, he remains a muhrim forever until he performs them. [739] (26) If he left four circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he will remain in ihram forever until he performs tawaf. If he did not do four circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, then he has not performed the majority of tawaf, so it is as if he did not perform tawaf at all. Therefore, unless he performs the obligatory tawaf, he remains in the state of ihram regarding his wife, because his wife is not lawful to him until he performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah. There is an athar from Abu al-Zinad from the jurists of Madinah that they used to say: whoever forgets to perform the tawaf al-ifadah... (footnote: Ibn Abbas said: whoever forgets or leaves something of his rites, let him shed blood).
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This lesson covers the severe consequence of omitting the majority (four or more) of the seven circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Since four circuits constitute more than half, the tawaf is considered incomplete. The person remains in a state of ihram indefinitely—meaning marital relations with his wife remain forbidden (as she is not halal until Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed). The ruling applies even if he has already completed other rites. The only remedy is to return to Makkah and perform the tawaf. If he cannot, he remains in ihram permanently, which has profound implications. The text references an athar from Madinan jurists supporting the principle that omission of the ifadah tawaf requires him to remain in ihram. A footnote repeats the general athar of Ibn Abbas about shedding blood for missed rites, but the main ruling here is unique due to the extent of the omission.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ritual consecration (ihram) for Hajj or Umrah, subject to prohibitions including marital relations.
طواف الإفاضة (tawaf al-ifadah): Same as Tawaf al-Ziyarah; the essential tawaf of Hajj performed after returning from Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person leaves four circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) He must slaughter a camel
B) He remains in ihram forever until he performs the circuits
C) It is acceptable because he performed more than half
D) He must repeat the Hajj next year

Key Takeaway
Missing four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah renders the tawaf void; the pilgrim remains in ihram indefinitely until the circuits are completed.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah in Janabah: Penalty and Remedy
Ruling for tawaf al-ziyarah in janabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the penalty for performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah and identify the condition under which the penalty is lifted.

Core Idea
A camel is due for Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah; repeating it in Makkah removes the obligation.

This passage from the matn addresses a specific violation during Hajj: performing the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah. The ruling establishes both the required compensation and the recommended remedy, highlighting the flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed while in janabah. The ruling is that a camel (badanah) is obligatory as compensation.
Janabah is major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
2
Note the recommended remedy
The better course (afdal) is to repeat the tawaf while still in Makkah. This removes the obligation of the camel.
Repeating after leaving Makkah does not lift the penalty.
3
Understand the consequence of omission
If the pilgrim does not repeat the tawaf while in Makkah, the camel remains due and must be sacrificed.
The camel is not waived automatically by returning home.
4
Distinguish the remedy's condition
The repetition must be done in Makkah. Repeating it elsewhere does not remove the penalty. This condition is essential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان جنبا فعليه بدنة والافضل ان يعيد الطواف مادام بمكة ولا ذبح عليه
And if he was in a state of janabah, then upon him is a camel, and the better course is that he repeats the tawaf as long as he is in Makkah, and no slaughter is upon him.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn on the consequences of performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in janabah. Since janabah is a major ritual impurity, the penalty is also major—a camel (بدنة). However, the better (افضل) course is to repeat the tawaf while still in Makkah; if he does so, the obligation of the camel is lifted because the deficiency is rectified. If he does not repeat it, the camel remains due.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
بدنة (badanah): A camel brought for sacrifice as compensation.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj, also called tawaf al-ifadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required compensation for performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in janabah?
A) A sheep
B) A camel
C) One-third of a camel
D) Nothing if repeated

Key Takeaway
Performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah necessitates a camel; repeating it in Makkah removes the penalty.

Compensation for Tawaf al-Sadr with Impurity
Differentiates compensation for tawaf al-sadr based on impurity type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation for Tawaf al-Sadr when performed in a state of minor impurity (hadath) versus major impurity (janabah) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Minor impurity in farewell tawaf requires sadaqah; major impurity requires a sheep.

This rule from the Hanafi school specifies the penalty for Tawaf al-Sadr (also known as Tawaf al-Wada') performed without proper purity. The amount of compensation escalates with the severity of impurity—sadaqah for minor hadath and a sheep for janabah. This distinction reflects the principle that greater violations require greater redress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf) is wajib in the Hanafi school, not a rukn. Its omission or defective performance triggers a compensation.
This is distinct from the obligatory tawaf al-ifadah.
2
Distinguish the two states of impurity
The source mentions two states: hadath (minor impurity, e.g., passing wind) and janabah (major impurity requiring ghusl). The compensation differs.
Janabah is a more severe state.
3
Note the prescribed compensation for each
For hadath, the compensation is sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat or equivalent). For janabah, it is a sheep.
Sadaqah here is a fixed legal amount, not general charity.
4
Understand the rationale
The heavier penalty for janabah is due to the greater violation. This is analogous to tawaf al-qudum, which has the same ruling.
The analogy is based on the principle of qiyas.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i school
The Shafi'i school requires a sacrificial animal (sheep) for any impurity in tawaf, making no distinction between minor and major.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both views are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن طاف طواف الصدر محدثا فعليه صدقة وان كان جنبا فعليه شاة
And whoever performs tawaf al-sadr while in a state of minor impurity (hadath), then upon him is sadaqah, and if he was in janabah, then upon him is a sheep.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This rule explains the penalty for Tawaf al-Sadr (also called Tawaf al-Wada' – the farewell tawaf) performed in a state of impurity. The level of penalty corresponds to the severity of impurity: minor impurity (حدث) requires sadaqah (which is a small amount of charity, typically half a sa' of grain or equivalent), while major impurity (جنابت) requires a sheep (شاة). This is analogous to Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf), which has similar rulings. The reason for the distinction is that janabah is a greater violation, hence a larger compensation.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed before leaving Makkah; also called طواف الوداع.
صدقة (sadaqah): Here it refers to a specific compensation: half a sa' of wheat or equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the compensation for Tawaf al-Sadr performed in a state of minor impurity (hadath)?
A) A sheep
B) Sadaqah
C) Nothing
D) A camel

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sadr in hadath requires sadaqah; in janabah requires a sheep.

Compensation for Missing Up to Three Shawts of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Compensation for omitting up to three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for omitting up to three shawts of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and identify the proof from the Sahabi athar.

Core Idea
Omitting up to three shawts of a fard tawaf requires a sheep; the tawaf remains valid.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a fard pillar of Hajj. Pilgrims may miss some circuits due to crowds or forgetfulness. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: if three or fewer circuits are omitted, the tawaf is valid but a sacrificial sheep is wajib. This lesson explains the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is omitting three or fewer shawts of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling is that a sheep (شاة) is wajib as compensation.
Tawaf al-Ziyarah itself is fard; omitting part triggers wajib compensation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' This is a Qawl Sahabi reported by Malik in al-Muwatta.
The athar is zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'something of his rites' (نسكه) includes all rituals, and tawaf is a rite. 'Leaves it' (تركه) covers omission of part or whole. Therefore, leaving part of tawaf requires blood (sacrifice).
4
Note the scope of the ruling
This ruling applies only when three or fewer shawts are omitted (i.e., at least four completed). If four or more are omitted, the tawaf must be repeated.
The boundary of three shawts is specific to the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the authority
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position (from the core Hanafi texts). It is the mufta bihi (operative) ruling. Other schools may have differing views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ترک طواف الزيارة ثلثة اشواط فمادونها فعليه شاة
And if he leaves three shawts of Tawaf al-Ziyarah or less than that, then upon him is a sheep.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This ruling covers cases where a pilgrim omits some circuits of the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If the omitted portion is three shawts or fewer (i.e., he completed at least four), the tawaf is still valid but a sheep (شاة) is wajib as compensation. The proof is the athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas (radiallahu anhuma) mentioned in the text: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' (موطأ مالك). Since Tawaf al-Ziyarah is fard, omitting part of it requires a sacrificial animal. Note: if he omits four or more shawts, the ruling differs (see next lesson).

Key Terms
شوط (shaut): One full circuit around the Kaaba; plural اشواط.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many shawts of Tawaf al-Ziyarah must be left for a sheep to be due?
A) Four shawts
B) Three shawts or fewer
C) One shawt
D) Two shawts

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, omitting up to three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah requires a sheep as compensation; the tawaf remains valid.
